<Author>LisaMaine_USA
<Content>Do not go here!!!!! Went on this 8 day trip with my 20-y/o daughter. I certainly will not go again. Some things we experienced:*Front desk very slow..........long lines to check in. Desk clerks spoke almost NO English, and very difficult to get their attention. Finally got to our room, to find it was not in the area/room I paid for. Returned to desk..........again, in line for about an hour........to be finally told that they were overbooked, and there was nothing they could do. We returned to our room, and I called Travelocity (a $45 call).....the Travelocity rep tried to be helpful, even 3-waying us into a call with the desk manager. We went back to the desk, and as we approached, David the manager we had spoken with, ran out the back door. When we asked to speak with him, we were told that he was not there. Checked with them several times during the week about a room change, which never happened.*The room.............nasty. Smelled mildewed, not very clean. Bedspreads were dirty. Slate shower cracked, moldy-smelling, and had a huge leak out to the rest of the bathroom. Toilet had virtually no flushing pressure; our toilet clogged every day. We returned from a day at the beach once to find the toilet bowl full of poop (not ours!!). It, of course, didn't flush, and we waited for 3 hours (including several calls and a trip to the desk) for this to be remedied. There was a hole above the sink which leaked dirty water onto the sink area; a steady stream when it rained (showers at night). The closet was moldy, and leaked heavily during rains...enough to pour out into the room. The floor of the room was constantly wet. Difficult to get clean towels.*The food...........tiresome. There are two buffets, only one is open for all 3 meals.....and it is the SAME FOOD EVERY DAY!!!!!!!!!!! Neither my daughter or I eat seafood or red meat, so we were outta luck with lunches and dinners. Did eat a lot of fresh fruit, which we liked. There are 3 other choices for dinner: a Mexican buffet (lots of mystery meat), a Japanese restaurant, which was delicious, and a Caribbean-style, which was delicious. Other than that, there are 2 other options: a pizza place (ick...the flies), and an outdoor grill on the beach..........serving the same thing every day..........hamburgers and fries, occasionally lettuce and tomatoes. All eateries except the Caribbean one are outdoors, or at least unenclosed from the outside. Thus, birds and bugs visited the buffets.......... buffets are pretty much a free-for-all, with adults and children alike pawing through the food (literally...bare hands!), eating off the serving trays, breathing and coughing all over the food, serving utensils, etc. People's manners were quite appalling. We resorted to safe foods.....individual yogurts, bananas, oranges. The natives..........for the most part, very welcoming.....we found that tipping regularly was VERY appreciated, and provided excellent customer service. These people are so poor....they appreciate the tips, especially with US dollars! The animation staff was fun........amazingly these young people spoke 6 or 7 different languages!! They are very willing to involve visitors in dance lessons, exercise classes, or just conversation.The tourists............very, very few Americans. Mostly European tourists, and we met some folks from Russia, Canada. One thing that really grossed us out was the fact that nearly ALL the tourists smoked. It seemed we we constantly breathing in second-hand smoke. They seemed to have no etiquette or consideration with their smoking...........they'd blow smoke right at you, on the beach, or while eating. RUDE RUDE RUDE. Lots of cigarette butts in the beach sand (yuck). If you are a nonsmoker, this will definitely disgust you.The beach.............the water was gorgeous!! Clean, clear, and deliciously warm. You can see right down to the bottom, even in very deep water. There is no surf here because of the reef.Very enjoyable playing and swimming. The sand on the beach is so soft and fine...almost like confectioner's sugar. The workers work hard to keep the sand clean, but they just can't keep up with all the piggy people who feel they can use it as a dump. The beach is littered with lazy tourist's crap.........discarded plastic cups, styrofoam plates, empty cigarette packs, condom wrappers (!), and lots and lots of cigarette butts. One morning I laid my towel down on the chaise, only to find it smeared with fresh [-].I could go on, but I think you get the point.............If you are going to take the time and spend the money to go to Punta Cana, PLEASE cough up the extra $200-300 bucks and go to a decent hotel!!!!Lisa  Raechel

There were some children there with their parents, but it was still awesome. we were there for 7 nights and it was the perfect length of time. BRING SUNBLOCK. We brought 3 bottles and still ran out on our last day. I was pretty well burned on the way home. It was all inclusive but i suggest bringing like 10 dollars in singles a day to tip. The staff there is very eager to please and they only make about $1600 a year in American money!! so tip well and you will be rewarded with a wonderful vacation. If you have never traveled to the DR be aware that when you get off of the airplane you will be swarmed by taxi drivers. I would highly recommend that you arrange your ride to the hotel ahead of time. The trip to the hotel was a little scary as there driving is a little different from us in the states. Do not buy cigars or alcohol from the beach vendors. the cigars are dry and usually fake. I bought my wife a necklace they asked $80 American for it. I ended up paying $15. It was fun to bargain with the people. Leave the house keepers tips and gifts. We brought a bunch of snacks for the airplane so we would leave cookies and chips with a couple of dollars for the cleaning people. on our 2nd to last night they covered our bed in flower pedals and made our bed up beautifully. I made a friend with one bartender. I tipped him well. about $80 total for the week and he hooked us up. I will not say any more, because I do not want him to get into trouble. DO NOT STAY NEAR THE BEACH STAY IN THE VILLAS. if you are unhappy with your room tell them that you requested to be in the villas and they will relocate you if they can. If you don鈥檛 speak Spanish be prepared to use body language. some bartenders and hosts speak a little English but it is a challenge to get your point across. also be prepared to wait a little longer than you would in the states. you didn鈥檛 go on vacation to New York, take it easy your in the DR. Hope you enjoy your stay.

<Content>Loved it Almost Perfect in every way !! Well what can I can and where do I start:Myself and 2 friends booked this holiday kinda last min and did do some research (read a few mixed reviews etc on here) and so were somewhat apprehensive...........we needn't have been though.Villas:After our 20 min transfer from the airport we were checked in very speedy and taken to our villa via a golf buggy thing as it was dark when we arrived we didn't get to see the gardens until morning but the outside of the villas  inside were fine for us three girls. We did have two double beds which wasn't what we expected but not a problem we took it in turns to have a bed by ourselves. It was all clean and all lights aircon shower etc were working the only thing we did notice was there was only one socket so we had to take it in turns to use phone chargers/ipod chargers etc again not really an issue.The Grounds:The gardens/ pool areas /food areas and beach we all very clean and kept to a high standard. Everyday there were people cleaning/sweeping etc and they all did it with a smile on thier faces and a hola to the guests. There was some construction work being done while we were there but that was at the other end of the complex towards the beach and nowhere near the villas so no noise disturbance at all. The 2 pools that were in action were lovely and the one that wasn't in sue due to building work looked great too one it is finished.Food:Myself and my friends are all vegetarian and we never had any problem with finding something to eat ...we found the local dishes were the nicest and the omlettes for brekkie really set you up for the day..... try to order things in spanish the chefs /waiters really appreciate it and you get a speedier response / service. We ate at all three of the pre-bookable restaruants and all were excellent The Carbie (Carribean) was the nicest for us and then Bambo (Japanese) and then Mexican. You book these at customer services in reception area oposite the check in desk.Beach:Oh my god it was beautiful we will never forget the moment that we walked through the beach grill onto the pure white sand through the many palm trees to the clear blue waters what a sight !! The beach was very clean and you could walk for miles along it . We didn't get a lot of hassle which compared to some places i've been to was suprising.....just a friendly Hola and no thank you is all that is needed.Other:All the staff are very welcoming and friendly yes this place is manily for europeans and the language is mainly spainish which we didn't find a problem... the dominicans are so relaxed if they say 10 mins you can be sure it would be an hour but that's all the fun.I would reconmend this place for and RR holiday which is just what I needed and a week was not long enough in fact we are going to book the same time next year !!Saona Island is paradise and would reconmend to anyone book with godfrey who is based on the beach 拢35 each for all transport there catamaran to island  speadboat back with food and drinks bargain !! although get insect repelant with at least 50% DEET in it as the mozzies are big there !!One last note is that you have def got to go to the spa it's gorgeous the full massage was fab and a quarter of the price in the UK.Any questions just email me.Many thanks to Edward our cocktail waiter, Fontus our spa man, Rolando our photographer  the girls on the catamaran all made our holiday even better !!Please remember that the staff do not get paid a lot and tips are welcome but not asked for....... we noticed how rude some of the guests are to them which was very uncalled for they all do thier upmost to make you welcome, they are very eager to learn english and we all spent many hours teaching the staff new words and vice a versa .... try to learn some spainish as it goes a long way......me and my friend are even going to take evening classes !!

<Content>Will go back tomorrow This is my second trip to Punta Cana and to IFA Villas, my stay Jul 21st to Jul28th 07 was as pleasant as usual very relaxing with some off the resort activities to take care of the boredom some folks have alluded to. My family had a great time although we missed the larger of the three pools that is undergoing renovation.Sure there is construction going on but you get used to it and it does not bother anyone, the hotel provided music to damper any noise that might annoy the guests, the most you will hear is a few hammers doing their thing, you got to be a winger to complain about this?Some of us should book trips to Florida because the last time I looked Punta Cana is in the Dominican Republic and their native language is Spanish and we are visiting a sorveign country. During my stay I encountered many members of staff that spoke English and even embrassed my wife who was trying to tell the waiter her order in butchered Spanish when he delightfully told her he spoke English.During my stay I noticed that tipping went a long way, the second day I tipped the cleaning lady $10.00 my room was always in tip top condition extra towels and the fridge always stocked with extra sodas and water even bottles of beer left on top of the fridge.These folks work 12 days straight 12 to 16 hour days and get 3 days off,most of them live in Santo Domingo which is 4 hours away by bus. On the topic of Santo Domingo I took the one day tour into this beautiful city organised by Pierto Tours we drove through two major towns of Higuey and La Romana saw how the locals live then to the cave of the 3 eyes ,a cave that have 3 fresh water lakes at the bottom of coral entrenched walls. Then on to the residence of Christoper Columbus, walk the halls of this great man and see his bedroom. a tour of the first Cathedral of the Americas. What a sight this was! Lunch provided at a posh resaurant by the harbor.Please be aware that when shopping in down town Santo Domingo have your bargaining hat on do not buy at the first price it gets cheaper when you are leaving to go home on the bus.Do the party boat run by Kontiki Tours they take you out off the shore of Punta Cana and you have a great time dancing to the sounds of Regge and meregue then off to snorkeling.Captain your own two man speed boat down the entire coastline of Punta Cana taking in all the resorts along the way and then off to snorkeling this is run by Aquatic Tours/ Bavaro Splash.The food at the Resort was plentiful and delicious also the food at the Japanese and the Mexican was excellent but you must make reservations at guest services and what's the problem with wearing a pair of slacks or jeans?The nighty entertainment and disco was great and it was something to look forward to at night I spoke to one of my friends who was staying at a more fancy resort and he said he did not have nightly entertainment and his resort was too crowded.Pack your bags and visit this resort.

<Author>Ilovedomrep
<Content>Hotel Ifa was great, some reviewers are just such whingers! I wish to write an optomistic review of Hotel IFA villas to give hope to people who have booked to go there and may be apprehensive having read some of these reviews. I have just returned with my boyfriend and had a fantastic time, I really cannot fault the experience, just a few minor issues that did not affect my holiday at all.Accommodation - Better than expected, very spacious, excellent air-con, well-cleaned and maintained daily by maids. Sheets and towels changed, water replenished. Perfectly fine.Transfers/Rep - Transfers comfortable and punctual, no problems. Rep from Hola tours excellent, provided all info needed, gave us his mobile no, booked trip on our behalf.Staff - Excellent. Don't expect a lot of english speakers but these people are sooooo hard working and very efficient and attentive as well as friendly. We recieved fast service and in restaurants water for example was constantly being topped up.Food - Main buffet restaurant had excellent choice and variety including stuff cooked in front of you, other buffet closed, I think not yet busy enough to use. Pizzeria gorgeous as was beach grill. The a la carte restaurants were fantastic. Very posh and served food you'd pay a fortune for over here. The oriental was my favourite.Pool - Main pool under construction. Didn't bother us as there were two others plus the beach. The main pool looks as though it'll be fantastic when finished. There was building work around the pool but with the music it wasn't noticable, plus the builders finished relatively early. Animation crew not my thing but were not persistant in trying to get you to participate which was good.Beach - Gorgeous. The best part. Lovely sand and clear to blue sea. A surprising array of fish are in the shallow areas if you go snorkelling. Overall: We had a great week and I can't imagine we could have got much better from any other resort. Our excursion to Saona Island was brilliant, well worth doing, the place is pure paradise. I could easily have stayed here for 2 weeks relaxing holiday although a few excursions would have been in order to add variety. Would definitely recommend and think it would be worth returning in a year or so when the work has been completed.

<Content>We Got Broken In To..... We have just got back from IFAVillas bavero. We had a room overlooking the main pool. There was building work opposite us and they would turn up the music so loud to drown out the constant banging. The other pool was better near to the spa nice and quiet. We got burgled on our 3rd day from going home, the front door had been broken open, they stole 2 mobile phones and a digital camera. Luckily we had the safe with everything else in, but could not fit it all in. The hotel guest relations luckily took us to the police station thank god as they never spoke a word of English. After that we had to carry everything around with us, which is not ideal. The hotel is definitely not a 4 star more like 3. The position of the hotel is excellent it just needs a complete re-furb! The room is very basic and lots of things are loose or hanging off! When we first arrived the patio doors did not lock but they sorted that out straight away, also there was mould growing in the bathroom . The people are really friendly. If your looking for a cheap hotel than this is adequate just make sure you do not take any expensive items with you. If we had not been broken into we would have had a really good holiday. Just wanted to warn people before hand.

<Author>mgustavyahar
<Content>Good Value for R  I just came back June 19th from staying at this resort. I can't say I have any complaints but I also can't write a rave review. I would have to agree with the previous review entitled Just Ok. All reviews have to be taken with a grain of salt. I am well traveled and have had many different experiences in Latin America. I also read many of the reviews on this site about this resort, which are accurate.Check-in: No problem. My friend and I met up two other female friends and at check in we requested that we be placed near each other. This request was taken care of without any problemStaff: The staff is very accomodating though sometimes reluctant. I found that I got everything that I asked for--extra towels, help with lost luggage, iron, new hair dryer, shuttle ride, birthday cake and song for friend--I just had to ask! Nothing was offered. Other reviewers are correct, the staff's confidence in their english abilities is not great. Most people in the DR were VERY grateful that I spoke Spanish and I think that really helped us enjoy our time there. FoodI found the food enjoyable. I always found something I liked at the Buffets. I actually preferred the Buffets than the specialty restaurants because I could eat my fill. I'm a big eater and I like variety. I am also a picky eater that tries to keep kosher and is lactose intolerant so variety is key for me. At the breakfast buffet there is an egg station which I enjoyed very much. Though it is called an omelet station you can order your eggs anyway you want. I always had them scrambled with the omelet ingredients. Other guests would hold gesture with their hands how many eggs they wanted and the chef would gesture when it was time to flip so no need to know sunny side up or overeasy in Spanish! Also, all the items in the buffet have signs in different languages so you can figure out what the item is. Only complaint about breakfast: no real orange juice. I think they used Tang power drink for the juice.Dinner Buffet had a grilling station and a pasta station along with other typical food items (including goat meat!). Specialty restaurants include a Mexican, Asian and Carribean themed restaurant. The Mexican restaurant is really a buffet with fajitas and tacos. The Asican and Carribean restaurant only allowed you to order one appetizer, an entree and dessert. This is why I didn't enjoy those restaurants. The sushi I had at the Asian restaurant was disgusting. it was supposed to be a salmon, avocado and cucumber roll. The salmon was COOKEd and the outside was drenched in a weird sweet sauce. The Grouper that I ordered came out very rubbery and disgusting. Two people in my group really enjoyed their experience there however. The Caribean restaurant was ok, with my dietary restrictions I could only order the chicken kebabs which tasted oddly like KFC original recipe fried chicken. AFter each meal I was still hungry which made me long for the buffet. The Jalisco and Caribbean restaurants are AIR CONDITIONED. The buffet was sometimes intolerable in the heat. You will sweat a lot during dinner! While outside there is a nice breeze, the breeze is not felt inside the buffet and the warmth of all the food stations can make it quite hot inside!The Pikalo restaurant by the Pool is amazing. The pizza is very very good and I ate there quite often. The Pizza place also serves nachos, chicken nuggets, fries and hamburgers! There is a bar/grill at the beach which serves a buffet and grills hamburgers as well. The Beach bar is the ONLY bar that serves Presidente beer. Everywhere else serves Brahma beer.Drinks: I was very disappointed with the drinks. Due to the heat, it was impossible for the frozen drinks to remain frozen after being poured. Add warm rum and you get a slushie drink. Also every drink, and I mean every drink, aside from beer was incredibly sweet. I could not stomach having more than two drinks. The beer was filling and became warm very fast. So my desire to have a pleasant buzz most of the time were dashed. I enjoyed the service at the High Beach Bar and the Capitan. The Pool bar staff was NOT friendly EVER. The beach bartender was also very friendly.Pool. The reviewers are right. There is a lot of construction but it didn't affect my enjoyment. The music is very loud and mainly merengue/latin which got tiresome after awhile. The pool chairs are limited. I enjoyed the beach a lot more because of the scene and the breeze.Beach: There are plenty of beach chairs around. I never found it necessary to get up early and reserve a beach chair, though in some instances we had to scramble for chairs in the shade. We went so far as dragging chairs under small trees. It is VERY HOT in the sun even for a sunlover like me who lives in Miami. I was shocked at how much stronger the sun is than in Miami. I was also shocked at how many pale skinned people stayed in the sun despite being bright bright red.Activities: I was shocked to discover how much everything cost in the DR. At every chance, people ask you for money. We did the Saona Island tour. Long Bus trip, then speed boats to island, and catamaran back. It was very nice except for all the chances you were given to spend money. After a guilt trip about the DR economy by the tour guide you get off the bus and are swarmed by people trying to sell you things. You land on the island and immediately people are aggressively pursuing you to buy hand made necklaces, get a massage, or have your hair braided. Also there was a person making a video of the trip and tried to sell you the dvd afterwards. Lastly, you were offered a bottle of rum for 13 dollars that had your group's picture pasted on the bottle. EVERYTHING fun seemed to cost money. Of the included water sports: Kayak, windsurfing, and sailboats, you had to leave a $30 deposit. Parasailing is $35 per person for 10 minutes. A banana boat is $6per person for 10 minutes. Snorkeling is free only if you want to snorkel in the swimming area where there is nothing to see. You have to pay between $25 to $30 for a trip out to the reef or a shipwreck.The animation guys could get quite annoying. They would often harass my friends and I to do stretching with them. We just wanted to be alone and relax but they were aggressive of shouting at us with a microphone or following us around with a yoga mat. All the male staff are quite forward and will let you know (if you are) that you are pretty, ask about your boyfriend or husband, and tell you that they love you. Some of the Beach Animation guys danced suggestively in front of us.Fun find: There is a photo shack at the resort with professional photographers. They walk around the resort with a monkey or an iguana and take pictures. Later you can go and look for your picture and purchase it for $8. Alternatively you can arrange a private photo shoot and they take you to various locations, including the beach, to take pictures of you. My girlfriends and I had fun pretending to be contestants on America's Next Top Model and we had some very lovely pictures taken of us. We all even had the audacity to take topless photos (we covered ourselves with our arms). I look forward to looking at these pictures 30 years from now with nostalgia about my youth! We saw pictures of couples and kids that turned out very nice! The pics cost $5 if placed on a CD or $8 if printed. The photographer will give you a discount if you have over 100 photos (which we did have with 4 girls).SPA. The spa is very nice but the prices are very similar to U.S prices. I had an 80 minute massage and enjoyed the steam room and sauna. I also received the worst pedicure ever, but the staff were very friendly and the SPA facilities were top-notch.DISCO: Opens at 11:30. Most of the time my friends and I were too tired to stay up and go to the Disco, particularly since we couldn't get a buzz from the drinks to keep the party going. I went to the Disco twice. It is on the beach but there is a shuttle from the reception area that will take you to the beach and drop you off at the disco. The disco plays some club favorites but it is mostly latin music. There is no air conditioning so it gets hot very quickly. Not many guests go to the disco and I found that there were a lot of 18-24 year olds. Also, the staff liked to go there and dance with the pretty female guests. The Pasta Stations chef would not leave me alone at the disco. I politely refused to dance with them and then after many rejections he continued to stand next to me and smile creepily at me. I finally had to be rude and ask my friends to get pasta for me the rest of the time I was there! It was annoying. Clearly being polite and smiling is an indication that you welcome advances from the men in the DR. The Disco is also the only place you can get food at night. All the food places close after 10:30 or so. ROOMS:I like my room. I stayed right next to the High Beach Bar: Rm. 1126. It is far, but if we got lazy we would hop on the train (golf cart-like vehicle). The beds are VERY firm, but I like them that way. Other reviewers have compared the pillows to a sack of cotton balls but I didn't think they were bad. The hotel is inexplicably stingy with towels and I had a hard time asking for extra towels, but they did bring me more. The AC is very cold at night when you are sleeping and I found that it helped to put on socks and extra clothes at night. I happy to find there was a TV that had American TV channels like TNT and CNN. Not that I watched much TV but it was nice to do before falling asleep at night. We had no problem with the water pressure. You do not get any wash cloths which was a problem for a friend who used Bullfrog brand sunscreen that was SPF 45 and quite thick. So she felt she couldn't get clean with just soap on her hands. Bring washcloths if you need a good scrubbing while bathing.The fridge was stocked every other day with bottled water and nothing else. Except one day, frustrated by our inability to get a buzz, we splurged on three six dollar bottles of Presidente and brought them back to our room. They were that expensive because they were bought at the hotel's shop and were also quite large.Overall ambience:If you want to do nothing else but rest and relax then this is the place for you. I got a little antsy however and wished there was more to see and do. There are little markets on the beach outside the hotels but the vendors are quite aggressive and try to put jewelry on you. Nothing has a price tag on it because they wait to see how much you want to buy before they give you a price. I've been to a lot of Latin American countries so I didn't find anything worth bringing home with me. I also spent over a hundred dollars at the spa and $90 on an excursion and $125 for pictures from a photo shoot. After that, all I could afford was staying in the shade on the beach! Because I spoke spanish I befriended some staff members who looked out for us. There were many French tourists as well so I had the chance to also use my French! It was shocking how few Americans there were at the resort. I had a nice relaxing time, but after 5 days, I was ready to DO something.MISCELLANEOUS: I had a horrible experience with SPIRIT AIR. My luggage did not arrive until the next day. I recommend packing an extra bathing suit, coverup and a few toiletries in your carry-on should this happen to you. At least you can lounge at the beach sipping a cocktail while you wait for your bags!Bring Dollars or Euros. I was only able to use my debit card at the SPA and the Spa had a $100 minimum. There is an ATM at the hotel but it doles out pesos. You are given prices in dollars but the hotel will convert it for you so you can get the requisite pesos out of the machine. You can also use dollars for buying souvenirs and paying for excursions. It also never hurts to tip the staff a dollar or two for good service. It will ensure that you get preferential treatment the next time. Learn some key Spanish and French phrases. It helps!

<Author>o84blondie
<Content>Had a great time! I just got back from spending 6 days here with my boyfriend and we had a great time. We arrived earlier than check-in time on Sunday so we just hung out at the bar and drank. When we were given our room, it was very nice and clean. Spend the $3 a day to get a safe in your room. The buffets were good and rotated food daily. There was usually no wait and we could walk in and eat whenever we wanted. The grill on the beach had really yummy food as well. The Japanese and International restaurants were very good (the Mexican restaurant was closed). One pool was closed, but I didn't even know it was there until the 3rd day of our trip, so it wasn't that big of a deal. There are 2 others to choose from, plus the beach. The villas section is being re-done (along with the closed pool) so they are really trying to be competitive with other hotels. We stayed in the 4000 section and found it to be pretty well situated. It was about 5 minutes from the beach and 5 minutes to the pool/food. We recieved 2 huge bottles of water in our cooler that were replaced when we ran out. Our air conditioner did have a slight leak which made the floor under it a little wet, but I was not about to turn it off! It was fine for what we needed it for. The entertainment was good. They walk around the pool trying to get people to sign up for darts or horseshoes, etc. They put on a show at night that was a little cheesy, but I'm glad we saw it. I know a little Spanish but found that I didn't even need it because everyone there knew at least 3 other languages (including English) to give us directions or communicate with us. All in all, a great first all-inclusive for us. No complaints...wish I was still there. :)

<Author>ugooli
<Content>Amazing time! Beautiful Place! Great People! Four of us, 2 guys and 2 girls, went to Punta Cana for the very first time and we all had a blast! We were there from May 17-24. I think that May was a perfect month to go because it wasn鈥檛 incredibly crowded.Did I hear someone ask about the beach? First of all, the sun is hotter there than I鈥檝e ever felt anywhere else. It鈥檚 humid as expected but fortunately there is a cool breeze that blows every now and then which is nice. The beach doesn鈥檛 have much of a selection of trees to hide behind but you鈥檒l find shade if you look hard enough. The sand was white and clean. The water was warm during the day and actually cooled just enough at night. It was nice to take a dip in the ocean at sunset. When going to the beach, you may want to park yourself close to the bar and restaurant. They don鈥檛 come to you for any orders. You have to go to them. The food at the beach is pretty good though! Everything鈥檚 grilled. And by the way, if you aren鈥檛 staying at the Ocean Village, it really is about a 5-10 minute walk to the beach. It鈥檚 a nice walk though. You鈥檒l never notice the distance. But if you really don鈥檛 want to walk, there is a beach shuttle that will bring you there. It鈥檚 parked right outside of the reception desk.As for mosquitoes and sand fleas鈥?I didn鈥檛 get one bite on me. I did apply some Repel with DEET when it was really humid at night. But for the most part, I wasn鈥檛 affected. I did see some people with bites around their ankles so just be aware that you may get bitten. I鈥檇 be more concerned with applying sunscreen, as the sun鈥檚 rays are intense.The main pool area was always crowded with people. Luckily, our room in the Villas had a balcony with the view of the pool. They play music for most of the day. And what a variety鈥?from Celine Dion鈥檚 鈥淢y Heart Will Go On鈥?to Antony Santos鈥?鈥淓l Chico Del Apartamento 512鈥? It was enjoyable nonetheless especially when the staff would dance with the patrons. The other pool next to the spa hardly had any people there. The bar was never full. The water is a bit deeper; 5 feet compared to waist deep in the main pool.The rooms were cozy. I didn鈥檛 mind that the drapes didn鈥檛 match the valance. The beds were firm. The pillows felt like they were filled cotton balls. We stayed awake most hours of the day and night so I fell asleep once I landed on my bed. The air conditioner blew out some incredibly cold air and if you turn on the ceiling fan as well, you鈥檒l wake up to an arctic winter. =) Cable television was hit and miss as was water pressure. There were a couple instances where water wasn鈥檛 available. It usually lasted only an hour or so. So just walk out the door and get a beer or Cuba Libre while you wait. Hot water was also a commodity. Take showers quickly because you may run out. You might also have to wait a couple minutes for water to heat up if you鈥檙e the first one in the shower. Once the water pressure is available, it comes out at you with a flurry. It鈥檚 actually quite amusing. Just talk to the person at the Front Desk or Guest Relations when you have a problem. The bathroom in general isn鈥檛 as bad as some other people have said. So what if there are really really tiny ants walking around with you. They don鈥檛 visit all the time and they鈥檙e so few. It also comes with a fully loaded shampoo, conditioner and soap dispenser. Also, an iron and ironing board aren鈥檛 included in the room, but you can always call and ask for one. They鈥檒l bring it right up to you. Why do you ask would I need an iron? The a la carte restaurants require men to wear collared shirts and pants to enter. Women don鈥檛 have a dress code.Mineral water is always there for you in the refrigerator. Leave a couple dollars a day on top of the refrigerator and you may get an extra bottle or two when you get back to your room.There were probably only a handful of us Americans at the resort. That really didn鈥檛 matter because everyone was very nice. Even though only one of us spoke Spanish well, they really made an effort to communicate with us as best as they could. Most bartenders and hosts speak English well.The animation crew was great. They work tirelessly and all hours of the day! You might see the same guy doing the workout session in the morning at the beach, a dance class by pool in the afternoon, and dancing on stage at the club in the middle of the night. It鈥檚 amazing how much they work and all with a smile. The staff works 12 consecutive days out of every 15 days. So please be nice to them as they work very hard to keep us happy.Know your hosts and hostesses by name. The same goes for your bartender and wait staff. They鈥檒l really appreciate it and you鈥檒l have a much more fun time there. They鈥檙e incredibly friendly and will do what they can to give you what you ask for. You鈥檒l be surprised how well they remember your drink and usual table.Aside from the one at the beach, there was only one buffet open while we were there. And only the International and Japanese restaurants were open as well. The other restaurants were being remodeled. It鈥檚 ok though because overall the buffet was the place to be. They do have a limited menu, as they almost always looked the same daily. However, there鈥檚 a grill and a pasta bar that you can go to for extra variety. They also have a wide assortment of fruit to choose from.The buffet only serves beer and refreshments. Juices are limited as well. The pool bar, the bar at the beach, and the Pikalo Pizzeria offer a full bar. The a la carte restaurants also offer everything. The international restaurant offers a wine list that you have to pay for. Most wines are Spanish or Chilean. But not a bad selection. I would defer from the house wine at the Japanese restaurant.The best bar had to be the Pikalo where they serve pizza. However, the music wasn鈥檛 much to be desired in the evening. Even after days of trying to convince them to play more lively music, they insist on trying to get you to sleep. I guess they鈥檙e telling you to take a nap because the disco starts at 11:30PM at the beach. The Pikalo closes at 10PM. However, the pool bar closes at midnight. The drinks aren鈥檛 very strong. But you should really try a shot of Mama Juana! It鈥檚 a local drink that you鈥檒l either love or hate. Or you may just acquire a taste for it like we did.By the way, it鈥檚 OK to use the competitor when going on excursions. They鈥檙e actually very friendly and they go out of their way to accommodate you on what you鈥檇 like to do and see. If you speak English only, let them know so that your driver that day will be aware of it.My advice鈥?come with an open mind. Eat and drink all you want. Don鈥檛 make small issues bigger than they seem. Enjoy your time outside of the room. Meet people because they鈥檙e very welcoming. You鈥檒l have a great time I鈥檓 sure!Hope this helped! Enjoy your time there!

<Author>Malc-66
<Content>Mixed Feelings Firstly this was booked as a last minute destination therefore cannot complain about the price.I have written and read reviews on this site before and it can take a long time get all the required details, therefore I will use bullet points so no trawling through many paragraphs.Location - Great, right next to the AltanticAccomodation - Pretty poor, outdated and not everything works, maintenance required almost constantly.Restaurant Staff - Very warm and accomodating, waiters sometimes go missing though.Bar Staff - Terrible, will only serve you if there are no Spanish speaking customers around. When they are the staff usually are talking to them and ignoring you.Entertainment Staff - Generally okay, the staff at the main pool have limitless energy and are about all day and night. Happy Boy is hilarious and Roberto loves himself.Entertainment Show Staff - Not bad although more could be done to involve non Spanish speaking audiences. They practice all day and put on a decent show at night.Reception Staff - Generally do not speak very good English but try hard.Food - Very good, better than many places I have been.Facilities - If all Restaurants had been open then I may be able to give a better review. As it was there were only three places open, the main buffet was very good and two A La carte , the Japanese was nothing like any Japanese food I have ever tasted, more like fast food and the Colonial, which was excellent. You have to book the A La carte at least a day in advance, the Colonial is definately worth it.Pools - There were three, the main pool which is very lively, a large quiet pool, which is very quiet and mainly deserted and a smaller quiet pool which is near the Sports Bar, which is a bit out of the way and where they provide Scuba lessons in 2 foot of water, this pool is ideal for children.Overall - This hotel appears to accomodate babies, children, young teens, 16-22 , 23-100. It really only has time for the 16-22 everything is geared for them. The male staff will try and chat up any female regardless of age, or the fact that her boyfriend/husband is at the bar/toilet/pool.Things to look out for - When you pass reception you will constantly be badgered to buy trips on various mechanical modes of transport, all day. American teenagers who apparently think it is okay to pour drinks and put out cigarettes in the main pool and generally make so much noise that you wonder if they have ever been allowed out on thier own before. On the beach there is plenty of things to do, just try and find a quiet spot with some shade away from the hoardes of sellers and hotel photographers, it is virtually impossible good luck. If you are in a 4000 numbered something room, be prepared to be awake until 3-4 am as the night club is on the beach and you are right next to it.

<Author>trex0967
<Content>IFA Bavaro is Awesome!! First things first. The people on this site that are dogging this place are obviously people who think they get the luxury of taking home with them on vacation. Then stay at home! I traveled alone and had a blast. See subjects/comments below:FOOD: The buffets were decent and plentiful with various dishes,breads,desserts, and fruits/veggies to choose from so each time you could make up a good meal. The themed restaurants were awesome. My fav was the colonial with the beef filet and shripm salad to start. The pizza buffet was great by the main pool. DRINKS: One word: Mamajuana!! This is a herbal blend fused with rum and honey and you drink it as a shooter. Too many and you are toast in a hurry. The rum drinks were great too and they will mix anything of your liking up with it. TIP: Be nice and drop a $5 spot on the bartenders by the bar closest to your room or near the main pool bar (Gri-Gri) and you will get great service and drinks. Ask for your drinks Fuerte style (strong) and they will hook you up. And please, get friendly and chatty with the staff. The d.r. people are lots of fun and very nice!!ACTIVITIES: The animation staff gets involved in all kinds of interactive things with the guests. Get involved!! You are on vacation!! They are great. This happens everywhere from the pools to the beach. BEACHES: Been around and love how vast and wide the beach is. White sand, blue water, 100ft tall palm trees. Enough said??PEOPLE: I met folks from all over the world. Get busy with the spanish before you go. You just need to know some basics. If I had french and spanish in the bag, I'd have met many more girls as I was traveling as a single but soon had a huge group I was hanging with from all over the world and we stuck together like glue.ROOMS: Some issues but no big deal. A/C went out but was promply repaired. Drop a $5 spot onto your housekeeper the first morning and tell her you need plenty of bottled water (which is great water/natural spring and mineralized) and she will hook you up daily. All bad reviews take note: You are in DR not home!!

<Author>monkeybooty
<Content>Descent Vacation for the Price This was my second time to Punta Cana and overall it wasn't a bad hotel. Sure, there were some problems; outdated rooms and limited selection at the buffet. Actually the biggest thing that bothered me was the limited number of Chairs on the beach and the VERY limited areas of shade... not good for a person who burns easily!The staff were very friendly, the drinks were good, and the entertainment was a blast (but you have to get involved!). Most of the clientele were french and spanish, so it's a nice relaxed european environment. My recomendations: Get to the beach early to get a chair and shade, take quick showers to avoid freezing, get a slice of pizza at the pizzaria (best pizza I've ever had), go on stage when they are looking for participants, and go with an open mind! It wasn't a bad hotel for the price.

<Author>CanadaJoJo
<Content>Amazing resort for the value! Sorry this is a long review but we were very happy with the resort! We just got back on May 5, 2007 from the IFA Villas Bavaro and we were extremely surprised for the value! I can't say enough positive about it! When we booked it we were a little unsure being rated as a 3.5 star. However, when we arrived we were pleasantly surprised. The place is HUGE. We have been to 4 and 4.5 star resorts in the past and this was by far comparable! Even with the language barrier (as English was difficult for many to understand and/or speak) we found ALL the staff to be amazing, pleasant, friendly, etc.! When we arrived at the airport, there were probably 5-6 if not more international flights that had just arrived so some time was spent waiting in an unorganized line get through their customs (which was painless). Then to baggage claim, again, quick and painless. The only truly negative issue with our trip was that our airline carrier (Sunwing) was horribly represented and we had to search for 5-10 minutes - lugging our own luggage at that - just to FIND our bus! There was no rep from Sunwing to greet us when we arrived at the airport (nor easily available at the resort) to guide us to the correct bus (which there were probably 50-100 or more and not lined up numerically). However, once we finally found it and were on it, the bus ride to the resort was nice and air conditioned. Oh, and don't be fooled if upon departure from the resort someone tells you the new depature section of the airport is airconditioned - it's not - it's just open with big ceiling fans.Check in at the IFA was quick and painless. Remember you are on Dominican time so 5 minutes can mean 15-30 (but by no means was that always the case), and you are on vacation so relax if things aren't as speedy as home. That's what vacations are for.We were upgraded from the Villas to next to the Ocean Village (directly in front of the Pizza Bar). The Villas are a fair but thoroughly enjoyable walk to the beach as we would walk to them at night. The walk is always enjoyable when you are usually sitting doing and relaxing most of the time. Our rooms, numbered 3425  3426, overlooked the back of the property which had a pond with ducks, birds, a small island  fountain. They were what we classed as a short jaunt to the beach (about 5-7 minutes) but we enjoyed every moment of it. And if you didn't want to walk, there was always the bus that would take you from the reception area to the beach about every 5-10 minutes. Although we didn't get to see the inside of the Villas, from the outside they were quaint and beautiful.The place is absolutely spotless! Groups of maids would scrub any andevery inch of the resort - if it wasn't sand, it was cleaned. The pool decks, loungers, public bathroom floors, walls, etc etc. were scrubbed each and every morning and the public bathrooms around the resort were constantly cleaned - maids were assigned to each one all day. The rooms too were well maintained. We had no problems - air conditioning worked great plus there was a ceiling fan if the air was too cold - go figure! Clean beds. All clean towels every day (however no face cloths but that's no big deal). Pillows were a bit to be desired (quite lumpy) but again, no big deal. We were able to sleep comfortably each night and it certainly wouldn't put a sour taste in our mouth about the place. No problem with noise.There were 4 pools of varying sizes that we saw and all were great. We spent all but one day on the beach. We had great weather every day - most days, if not all, felt like it was 100 degrees (very humid)! It rained a couple nights for about 5-10 minutes but nothing to ruin our stay. Remember you can't predict mother nature. Even the Dominicans say you just can't predict their weather. If you want to hit a market, there were two that we found near the resort. Once on the beach and facing the ocean there is one immediately to your right. The market is much larger than it looks from the beach. We suggest hitting the back of it first (just walk along a path to the farthest vendor then go in). The back booths contain mostly clothing and trinkets as the personnel there are MUCH less aggressive. The front of the market (facing the beach) is very aggressive with vendors selling jewelry, Mamajuana (a local drink), cigars, liquor, coffee, etc. The other market is about a 5-10 minuteswalk along the beach to the left. It too is much larger than it appears and they too are very aggressive. Barter hard! They far overprice everything. Cut price they give by at least 75%. Shop on the resort first to get a price idea as the market starts much much higher. Then you have to bargain hard to beat the price down. The harder you bargain, the much better you. When you walk away they bargain even harder. Don't be afraid to do it. We found most items onthe resort shops to be the same price that you had to barter for at the market! For excursions, parasailing, etc. we dealt with Renaldo Cheapy Cheapy(or Orlando - difficult to understand). He is a petit gentleman with a gotee who wears a small black floppy hat with the edges frayed and sat at a hut next to the market  beach grill on the beach. He was awesome to deal with and we recommend him. The food was good. In the buffets the breakfast didn't change up much each day but there was certainly plenty to choose from between buffet stuff or grilled items. If you got tired of the buffet for lunch, there was the pizza bar or the Rancho beach grill. The beach grill had great food for lunch - chicken nuggets, hamburgers, chickenburgers, fish, pasta, french fries, crepes, etc etc etc!. The pizzaria had awesome pizzas to pick at but beware of the heat pizza. We had no problems with food. Yes, selection didn't change a whole lot but again, plenty to choose from that you could change it up yourself.Entertainment staff worked from about 10am to midnight every day. Very active and entertaining. We went for total RR so didn't do any excursions.I could write more but my fingers are getting tired. All in all, we loved the resort and would certainly return to it if we had the opportunity. I haven't had time yet to download my pictures so unfortunately I have none attached.  
<Date>May 7, 2007

<Author>springmounties
<Content>Before you book, please read! We just got back from one week stay at the IFA. I read all the reviews and couldn't understand why some were great and some were not. Now I know. The hotel has an old section and a new section. The old section is on the beach side where we stayed in the 3000 block. The bathrooms were in bad shape.Bathtub was rusted, small ants were all over the vanity and the ceiling leaked when it rained. The furniture was in poor condition, the bed was hard, but wasn't bad. The pillows felt like they were stuffed with cotton balls. Our balcony faced construction and machines were making noise for half a week.Bring washcloths!!! Our refrig was defrosted and we were expected to clean up the water afterward. It was only stocked with water until the last day, then we got beer and soda. The food was okay, but better at other resorts. My husband was somewhat disappointed with the food. The 3 special restraunts were nothing special, Japanese was the best. The drinks were okay, they would make them strong if you wanted them. (And left them a tip.) Not many spoke english. But it is a spanish speaking country, so learn alittle spanish already.Grounds were beautiful. Beach was a little further walk than other resorts we have been at. But it was beautiful. Employees seemed friendly. Entertainment was weak, but the effort was great.Check in and out went fine. If you go make sure you book in the new section. It's very nice over there, but a further walk to beach. They run bus shuttles back and forth often.Overall I wouldn't recommend this resort. I have been to better and it wouldn't take much for them to update the rooms and buffets.Pools were in good condition and clean. We wouldn't go back unless we booked a room in the newer section on the street side.

<Author>CCJ57
<Content>Asi Asi If you've never been to an all inclusive, I'm sure you would find IFA more than adequate. However, having been to several other resorts in the past, I was a bit disappointed with IFA Villas. The ROOMS were outdated but OK. As warned beforehand by other TripAdvisors, water pressure not good and we had no shower one night (I used the outdoor shower by the beach). The resort is very large and it is a bit of a walk to the beach. DO get your towel on a lounge before 9:00, either by the pool or on the beach. FOOD was OK - not great; not enough variety on the buffets and disappointing salad bar (again, compared to others I've been to). DRINKS very weak and watered down. Five shots of tequila and barely a buzz (normally one would do me). Staff not very friendly with the exception of waiters/waitresses. Apparently the week we were there was spring break for Europeans - loud partying throughout the night and security would do nothing. Surprised to see many changing their clothes on the beach. Topless not unusual, but I've never seen this before. Despite this mostly negative review, I reiterate it's not that bad if you've never been to other resorts to compare it to. Would I go back? Probably not unless it was a really good deal.

<Content>IFA Villas and Village Punta Cana Just got back from 1 week at the IFA VILLAS Punta Cana. 3 couples went together and we got an easy upgrade to the Village area without even asking for it! I couldn't stay up past midnight any ways. The pool music was above average and the beach music was very good too! Didn't take any tour other then the reef snorkling for 2 hrs for $20.00 was nice and we stopped off to see the shark and moray eels caged area also. The shops were the type you had to bargain for but since I was there 4 other times I knew all the angles and made great deals for myself and others. I usually too 75% off of 1st pricing then added more items and got great deals for around 60% off of starting prices. I don't know where the other reviews said the drinks were watered down because ours were very strong and if you just got shots they would knock you quickly. A few times depending on what bar you went (as there were 7 bars) they did do a few virgin drinks but I think it was just mistakes as the bartenders were very busy at all times. I would definitely recommend anyone to check out the deals at IFA VILLAS VILLAGE RESORT if size is not important to you, although this 1 was not too small but easiel to get around. I f money is not of a concern to you they this would not be the place for you! Costed us total: insurance, taxes, and all inclusive of $875. for 1 week where the larger resorts would cost you $1200-$1400. per person at this time of year. Hope I helped all! Wilddog

<Author>dominicanrum
<Content>Great Vacation, Great Value, Great Atmosphere Non stop fun the whole time we were in the Dominican Republic. Eight of us went and everyone agreed the resort was great. The resort is a great deal. The rooms and grounds were very clean. The food was good and a lot of variety. We ate at all three ala carte restaurants. The Mexican and Japanese we're great. We didn't enjoy the International restaurant.The animation team is a blast. Out on the beach in the morning and midday (stretching, dance lessons, water aerobics). Around the pool in the afternoons and early evens (different contests daily). Great shows nightly. They finish off each night at the discotecha.Henri, Robert and Chocolate (animation team members) are all great. If you get a chance, talk with them. You will be laughing the whole time.The beach is beautiful. Powder white sand and some large coral rocks at the edges of the swimming area. The are all kinds of fish swimming around the rocks. Watch out though, the sun is very strong and you will burn easily. We went on two excursions. Shopping($20)- Visit two shopping areas, cigar factory and rum factory. It's about 4 hours and very fun. Bring some cash and get ready to barter.Saona Island($80)- This is a whole day excursion. Totally worth the $80. Start with an hour and a half bus ride. Long but our guide talked to us most of the trip about the Dominican Republic, their history and you get to see how they really live. Then we got onto catamarans and sailed another hour and a half out to the island. On the boat you get drinks brought to you, dance with staff or just relax on the hammocks. On the island they grill out a great lunch and have an open bar. Delicious food. Relaxing on the island is no problem. There are beach chairs and hammocks everywhere. We rode speed boats back to the port, stopping on some sand bars to swim and see star fish. They whole excursion is unbelievable. I would recommend this resort to anyone and will hopefully be going back next year. Anyone looking for a great time stay here.

<Author>dmvan
<Content>Can not wait to get back there!!! I can't believe people 'poo-poo' this place. It was great! I was a little taken aback at the airport by the Dominican's curt nature at first but soon realized...I'M IN ANOTHER COUNTRY WITH A DIFFERENT CULTURE! Geez people, get real! There were couples, singles and families when I was there and ALL seemed to be having a fabulous time! The hotel and rooms have their issues but the fun, the weather and the overall experiences far outweigh any flaw in the rooms (which, if you are vacationing like most people, you shouldn't be in very much anyway) or delayed drink service. My only regret is that I didn't stay longer.Please... always research where you are planning to travel and how the people live, work and behave in that country. If you want to eat with gold plated cutlery and have the locals kiss your feet, this is not the place for you. Go somewhere else and let the rest of us have a great time here!

<Author>AgentAgii
<Content>Good Value for the money This Hotel is a good value for your dollar. The rooms are a little outdated but if you ask for a change they are very accommodating. The resort itself it Huge and has a vary nice beach and very nice pools. Plenty of places to eat and plenty of bars with great drinks. The resort is lively great animation team, entertainment everywhere and lively music. The nice touch is the bar in the villas section with Jacuzzi's around it for a nice relaxing afternoon. Surprisingly the Japanese restaurant was my favorite it was amazing they were really on point as far as Japanese food and decor I was really pleasantly suprised. Great service all around, and for the people complaining about Spanish speaking staff HELLO you are in a Spanish speaking country next time go to FLORIDA. As far as excursions go I will defiantly recommend cave fun it is an extreme sport excursion and defiantly not for kids or elderly. It is hard to find because only a few representatives offer it but it is defiantly worth going through the trouble of finding it. you drive about 2.5 to 3 hours but it is worth every minute of the drive upon arrival you are given breakfast fruit coffee and fresh juice and are geared up and introduced to the horses which take you on a 30 minute ride through the national park towards the cave. from that point on you hike through the national park for about 45 Dominican minute and you reach the cave. When you do reach the cave the only entrance point is a block hole that's about 60 feet deep and you have to be dropped on a line and little by little escort your self down in total darkness just with the little light on your helmet but the view is amazing. Then you get to explore the cave and it is Huge with beautiful lime stone droppings and beautiful under water streams that you get to swim through and at one point even dive and swim under the tunnel it is total amazing. When you finish exploring and hicking through the cave (about 2 hours) your horses are waiting to take you back to the ranch where you have an amazing Dominican lunch and a cold beer or soda. The excursion is the best I have ever done and I would recommend it to anyone the guides on it are wonderful and full of information. I will definatly be going back to visit Dominican Republick because it is a beautfiull country full of wonderfull culture and people.

<Author>kjkroll18
<Content>Average Hotel but still a lot of Fun My husband and I just got back from our 7 day vacation to Punta Cana (Feb. 16-23) and we stayed at The IFA Villas Bavaro Resort. At first we wondered what we go our selfs into when we walked into the resort.. because it looked so small...then we realized there was 3 parts to the resort and it actually is very big. Our room was average.. nothing fantastic. The pools were great for the most part and they had decent entertainment around the villas pool area. The beach was BEAUTIFUL! It was a little bit of a walk to the beach because the resort is big but definately worth the walk..thats where we spent most of our days. The food at the buffets are average..it took me a couple days to get use to because everything has a bit of an odd taste. But again not horrible. Dont even bother with the Mexican, Seafood, or Japenese restraunts.. they were horrible. All you get to drink is water there...we asked for soda or beer but never got it at any of those restraunts. The portions at these restraunt could probably not even fill up a 6 year old because they are so small. I just wouldn't bother wasting your time in those restaunts...And be sure if you decide to make reservations at any of those restraunts.. go at least 3-4 days a head of time to get a good reservation. Otherwise you may not even get a reservation or you wont be able to eat until 10pm at night. The only thing we really found horrible was probably only 3% of the vacationers and staff spoke english...we were so lonely and it got extremely fustrating not having most of the staff understand us. The employees spoke spanish and french mostly very very little english. We would recommend going with friends or family members to Punta Cana because if you think your going to meet english speaking people down there.... think again. We didnt meet someone who spoke english until our 2nd last day. So honestly that was the only thing really hard to deal with. Overall the hotel was ok/ average... if you get a good deal to stay here then its worth the money.

<Author>Randy83
<Content>Very Nice Vacation Just got back from two weks at this resort. First of all, the cleaning staff are amongst the hardest working I have ever seen at an all-inclusive (I've been to four now). They are always sweeping, cleaning and maintaining the grounds. I stayed from Jan 25 to feb 08, 2007. My room was 1180, and it was very nice. I had no problems with the air conditioning, I did have a problem getting a remote for my tv the first couple of days, but after getting Jennifer (the AirTransat rep )involved, this was quickly fixed. The hot water was iffy from time to time, but when it did work it worked just great. The food was very good the first week, but after the staff turnover in the second week, it fell off just a tad. I didn't hear of anybody getting sick, and many told me they were eating the salads as well. The wait staff at the bars need more language training as a rule, but if you just show up with a smile, and Hola Amigo, you should do just fine. I personally don't like the beach animation stuff, and if you don't either, if you turn to your right when you get to the beach, and walk past the Barcelo wharf for about another ten minutes, there is a beautiful area that is open to all the resorts, that is hardly used at all, very quiet, the waves are a lot softer and the beach is a lot cleaner, I higly recommend this area for those wanting a little romance during their vacation. The beach at the resort is very, very busy. Lots of motorboats, and all other types of beach fun, for a cost of course. There are a lot of sales people at the beach all day long. They aren't very forceful at the resorts area, but if you go past the resort area, they tend to be more forceful and pesky. All in all I loved my stay, the AirTransat reps were very good. I would definetly go back again. Randy, London Ontario, Canada

<Author>eez247
<Content>Great! I will post this review under both the IFA Villas and IFA Village as they are part of the same resort complex.Overall this resort is above average and I would rate it a four out of five.My girlfreind and I (both 27) arrive on JAn 29 and stayed until Feb 5, 2007.Facilities:Upon arrival they put us in the Villas section, room 1089, I asked them if they could move us closer to the beach and they said they would have a room in the 4000 block on the 31st.THe VIllas section is quite a ways away from the beach. The higher your room number in the 1000 block the further away you are. Overall my room in the Villas section was a little run down compared to the room I was given later in the 4000 block. I the worst problems were the shower( no tub) was very low flow and took a long time for the water to turn hot. Also the refrigerator did not seem to cool very well even on high. The TV had no remote and the front door did not seem very secure. I would recommend everyone to rent a safe ( $3 dollars a day) The Villas overall wuold be good for someone who would prefere a quiet location pool site rather then a crowded beach. Or the foot traffic of the other more central pools.The main stage, 3 al cart restaurant , a pool bar and Captain lounge are all located in the Villas section. The 2 buffet restaurants are located in the other parts of the complex so they are bit of a walk to get to.On the January 31 we moved to our room in the 4000 block in the Oceans Village section (4036). The room overall was in much better shape the our other room in the Villas The biigest improvement was the flow of the shower. The TV had a remote and as we were on the third flow we had a balcony. We were now only a short walk from the beach.The beach was great but make sure you wake up early and put a towel on a chair. Many days we slept in and could not find an empty chair and had to go over the Barcelo section of beach.Find the stage and stay away from it if you prefer quite as they like to blast the music.I found the grounds were very well kept and secureFoodOverall the food was very good. You could aways get something to eat from 7 Am to 3AM. The buffets offer an abundance of different foods. They always have someone on the grill cooking something. My personal favorite was breakfast, the cook woould prepare an omelette for you from an assortment of ingredients for your selection. My only complaint would be that sometime the waiter or waitress would take too long to get my drink and I'd be finished eating by the time it arrived. I only ate at the International a la carte restaurant so I can not comment on the other two. Many days I would grab a slice of pizza from the snack bar beside the pool in the Village section.The disco (afterhours at the beach bar) was somewhat of a disappointment as it was not very well attended. But you can go there to grab a bite to eat up until 3AM. Staff and entertainmentOverall the staff were very freindly. I never had any problems getting a drink. Sometime I'd go up to the bar and be asked what I wanted by three different bartenders while the fourth was alreadty preparing my order. If you are sitting at a table the waitresses can take some time coming around so I would have to go to the bar to get another drink.( No big deal) The Animation team (entertainment) was very good and they try to keep you entertained. AtmosphereThe week I was there the resort was mostly attended by couples and European tourists (mostly French). Although I did see many different combinations, groups of women , groups of men, some families etc I would definitely go back again.

<Author>to_traveller416
<Content>Good resort on a budget Four of us in our 30's stayed at this resort the week of January 21, 2007. I was a little sceptical since we paid very low price for our vacation and the resort is rated as 3 1/2 stars. The flight was good although a bit cramped, we flew Sunwing, and I would suggest to pay a little extra and have a pre-booked seat with a bit more leg room. Resort is very close to the airport, less than 15 minutes drive. Originally, we were booked into Villas part of the resort which is quite the way from the beach, and consists solely of bungalows. The resort was full but we slipped $15 to the girl at the reception desk and got rooms on the second floor in the Village part. Rooms are very clean and the maid service is immaculate. They did come to clean the rooms a bit early in the morning, before 9am, but if you hang 'do not disturb' sign on your door they will come back later. My only complaint in regards to the accomodation is that the walls seem to be paper thin. I could hear my friends talking in the room next to us.The food is great. There is a lot to choose from and everything is really tasty. Lots of fish, calamari, etc. Pasta grill is amazing, altough there is quite a line up every night but it's worth it. We usually ate breakfast and dinner at the main restaurant, and lunch at the beach grill. We visited the Mexican and Japanese a la carte restaurants, and I advise you to reserve your seats the moment you get to resort. We came back the next day and could only get the table at 10:30 at night. Mexican is buffet style, with excellent food, but Japanese restaurant is really out of this world. Amazing atmosphere and food to satisfy even someone who is not too keen on Japanese cuisine. Do not try red wine anywhere - it tastes like vinegar!! White wine is slightly better. The service at the restaurants is slow, to put it mildly. We would order a drink when we arrive for dinner, eat, and just when we were getting ready to leave the drinks would arrive. But this is a part of the deal - slow service seems to be expected in the Carribean. The bars were no better - the only decent one is 'El Capitain' adjecent to the Villas part of the Resort. Altough it's a good 10 minutes walk away from the beach it's definitely worth the walk if you want a decent coctail. Also, capuccino and espresso was only available at this bar, so that made it a bit hard for me as '3-cappucinos-per-day' person. You would see the machine on the other bars, however the staff would politely tell you it's broken and will be fixed tomorrow. That never materialised.The beach is absolutely gorgeous!! It's breathtaking, that's all I can say. There is no shade though, and you have to move your towel or lounge chair around every 15-20 minutes chasing a bit of shade from the palm trees. Get there early to secure your lounge chair, otherwise you would have to wait until late afternoon before one becomes available.All in all, this is an excellent resort for younger couples or singles. There is lots to do, lots of friendly people to meet, and even with a few shortcomings I would definitely go back and recommend this resort to friends.

<Content>loved the beach Me and my husband loved this resort.To start with yes, there is a little bit of a walk from some of the rooms to the beach,but you get a chance to take some great photos.The food isn't great in the buffet,the other three are good.try the steak in the international.The rooms are decent we had double beds.Housekeeping was good we left a 5 tip on the first day and didn't have to ask for anything else except extra pillows.The beach is sooo sweet we lived out there (i will include photos) my only complaint you have to leave a deposit to use the hotels water eq..We decided to go to the mall one day the cab ride was 70.00.I would advise people to share cab rides to cut down on the cost.The disco was fun on our second night there was a live band ,it's only on fridays.The entertainment was so-so.Sometimes you just wanna hear the waves ,music plays almost all the time it goes off at about 3am.Rain comes in intense showers but they only last about 15 minutes at a time.The drinks were a little watered down at 2 of the four bars.I think that we would go here again,there were a lot of kids ,a few were naked.Yes people were topless but you really do get use to it.I even got bold and went topless in the water.so for what we paid 1500.00 for 2 people for 8 days we had a ball.Be sure to try the snorkelling trip it's only 15.00 and it last for a hour.hope this helps.

<Author>Richju
<Content>Dont listen to the whingers!! If you are looking for a caribbean holiday on a smaller budget then this is the way to do it!! Our family (me, hubby, 2 girls aged 11 and 8) had the perfect 1st taste of the caribbean!! The whole resort is great and the beach will take your breath away!!Fabulous place, rooms are superb. Cleaned daily to a high standard, we never had cause for complaint. The whole resort is spotless, staff cleaning up constantly from those who cannot even be bothered to put a plastic cup in the bin instead leaving them to blow around or left on the islands in the pool!! (small moan I know but then these same people are generally the ones who complain!) The food is great in all restaurants, plenty of choice at breakfast, lunch and dinner. The Japanese is not very Japanese though! Only meal in 2 weeks we didn't enjoy. A couple of people had upset tummies but we put this down to the fact they were cleaning their teeth with tap water (a big NO NO!!) We, and several other families we met had no problems at all. Take LOTS of US dollars, it seems to be the currency they prefer. Peso's have little value. Resort shops are very expensive (if you have children and you need to-stock up with sweets and crisps before you go as there are no inclusive ice-creams) Some staff are rude-some are not-same anywhere in the world. Entertainment is repeated after the 1st week (think most go for 1 week!) Book trips, see some of the island, although fantastic, inclusive live can get boring......Definately give this place a go and make up your own mind!! The Victor Meldrew's are not always right you know!!

<Author>fairplay
<Content>Had a great time Just back from a week All Inc at this hotel. The hotel itself was lovely. the Beach beautiful. 3 pools to choose from catering for all tastes eg. one with full entertainment for the more energetic, one quiet and relaxing, one just rather small!The evening entertainment was really aimed at the under 14 age group and there is limited tabled seating (only 3 tables which would give you a view of the stage the rest is just chairs in rows in front of the stage)- shame as even cheesey entertainment i can enjoy but would always want a table to put my drink on!The room was always clean. We liked the fact that the maid didn't arrive until early afternoon as this meant we didn't have to rush out in the mornings like you do in some hotels.Food - fine if you're there for just a week. Any longer than that and you may get bored. This isn't due to the lack of variety as there is plenty there, it's just that with so many cultures visiting there is often only a few things you would be prepared to eat yourself. I like to try foods from different cultures but very little actually appealed.No children around as far as we saw, age range seemed to be mainly 20-40.We didn't come across any rude staff, and when our air con unit started dripping the engineer appeared within 5 mins of phoning reception.Even tho the above may sound negative we still had a really good time as all we were after was a week relaxing in the sun which is exactly what we got. I'd definately recommend it if that's all your after.
