<Author>CRAZEECAZZA
<Content>a GR8 time at IFA Bavaro - Essex, UK Visit 1 Aug to 14th Aug 2006 Life is what you make it !! - How can u not enjoy your hols - 2 families - with children aged 16,15,14 and 12 - 2 boys  2 girls. I think I speak for us all and say that we had a gr8 vacation at IFA Beach Villas.Rooms We were in the Villas section - which is the furthest away but they were really clean - didnt see a bug in our rooms for the whole 2 weeks. No mozzi bites either - but we did use Aftersun with insect repellent in it which was good. Beds comfortable - Air con fantastically cold - used to have it on really cold while out and turn it up to about 65/70 whilst we slept - which was comfortable - it would have been too cold to sleep - the air-con was that good. Maid service good - clean towels on our return every evening - beds made and room all cleaned with 2 bottles of water in our fridge every day and a flower left by the maid - all for a $1 tip in each room. By the way the walk to the beach - 12 mins stroll ( if u didnt stop at the Capitans Bar for a coffee or the Margarita for a Banana Mumma or a Cuba Libre in the middle pool bar.) The walk was beautiful through palm trees and flowers and a cheery hola and a smile from any staff u met along the way.PoolsThe one nearest us at the villas is the biggest, prettiest and probably the quietest with a lovely Margarita Bar in the middle.Great Banana Mummas, and Bloody Marys. Staff are smiley, sweet and friendly. El Capitan Bar does gr8 coffees and beers and is really relaxing. Middle Pool is livlier - gr8 Cocoloco party and we often stopped off on the way back from the beach in the evening for a last swim and a game of Volleyball with all nationalities in the pool. By the way there weren't many english people when we were there - but it was gr8 to meet people from all over the world - we met some lovely American people and Canadians - italians etc - our boys loved playing Volleyball with them all. Everyone just seemed to wanna have fun. we did a sort of bar crawl from villas to pool to bar to pool and off to the beach and the same on the return.BeachAbsolutely beautiful big, wide pure white sand nestled amongst hundreds of tall palm trees - they dont give much shade from the v hot tropical sun tho!!! The beach goes on for miles in either direction - did go for long walks down the beach and took a bottle of water with us. Entertainment on the beach in the morning - they didnt force u to join in - but it was gr8 fun having Merengue Lessons on the beach and water aerobics in the sea - cant do that in Essex. - hey join in now and again its a gr8 laugh. After a few activites - i got a bottle of water and took off down to a quiter part of the beach laid under a palm tree and read my book. Gr8 snorkelling just off the beach - better if you go out on a boat as lots of speed boats go up and down. Kids got canoes out - which was a bit like hard work - we hired a Hobby Cat out quite a few times for $20 for an hour ($100 deposit) that was great - sailed all the way down the beach. Walked down the beach for about 3 miles on a couple of days - it gets more and more deserted as you go past the AI hotels - its just paradise.WeatherReally hot, fantastic weather - always a breeze on the beach - found it too hot around the pools in the middle of the day - but be careful by the sea - u would never know how much you are burning. We hardly had any rain - one cloudy day but still real hot and a storm one afternoon which lasted about an hour and then the sun came out - liquid sunshine!! -FoodPlenty of it - we didn't get bored - thought the best buffet for breakfast was the one nearest the beach as it was so lovely to sit and look through the Coconut Grove towards the beach and sea and there was a lovely breeze there too. Manuel did wonderful made-to-order Omelettes whilst he sang and danced and smiled (or laughed ) as I tried to order in Espanol!!We tried all 3 Speciality Restaurants - staff were really polite and smiley - we thought the Caribe was the nicest - but they were all good. We did all have a touch of holiday tummy - none of us had to go to our beds - it didnt spoil the day - it only lasted no more than a day - just took a tablet of Immodium and were fine - probably just us adjusting to hot hot sun, lots of cocktails and fizzy drinks maybe a bit of jet-lag and of course a different diet.None of us were sick - there is a chemist on site which seems to sell everything and a 24 hour doctor - but hope u wont need them.By the way we all had ice in our drinks all the time. but we brushed our teeth in bottled water and drunk bottled water at all times. Us adults also had salad - I especially love my salad and ate it all the time.EntertainmentThis was mainly by the Villas Pool which consisted of Bingo early on in the evening - not our cup-of -tea - then fun and games which our kids thought George and his animation team were really funny. L8r they had Dancing Shows - the dancers are really fantastic - this did repeat on our 2nd week tho. We loved the music - and joined in the Club Dance on stage which happened at the end of every night's entertainment - The Latino - which you cant get out of your head - Im still playing it at home - we bought the CD and I just wish we were back there when I listen to it.TripsWe did the Speedboat/snorkelling trip - our boys loved driving the speedboats and the snorkelling was fantastic out on the reef. Our guide took some gr8 fotos of us under the sea whilst we were feeding the fish - lovely tropical coloured fish just eat right out of your fingers. they dont bite tho! Also did Katamaran Party trip - gr8 fun, rum, party and dancing - really funny guy on the boat - such a character.Beach Bar/ Beach DiscoLovely gr8 big bar and restaurant on beach - gr8 fries, lovely fruit and salads - garlic vegetables, burgers, salad snax etc on the beach in the daytime. Gr8 service from Ramone and Francisco - our men tipped them now and again and we were rewarded with great service - every time we looked up over came another beer or cocktail and a gr8 big Dominican Smile for us!!We did go to the Beach Disco on a few nights which didnt start till 11.30 - our 12 year old found it hard to stay up - but it was worth it - gr8 music - just makes u wanna get up and merengue! - how fantasic to dance under the moon and stars surrounded by palm trees and a breeze coming off the sea to cool you. What more could u want! I hope my review helps you - as before we came out I read some bad reviews as well as good which I felt was a bit off-putting but I can honestly say we had a fantastic time - It wasnt 5 star luxury - but we didnt pay for 5 star - it was great value for the 拢 or $ as the case may be.All in all we had a gr8 time - didnt want to go back to the Uk - couldve had another week. but then I always could! I would stay there again - but I feel you can never relive a gr8 time the same again and I like to visit other countries. This is my 4th trip to the Caribbean and I think the Dominicans are among the most friendly.TipWe took about $100 in $1 notes purely to tip them every now and again. I believe if you treat people with the respect they deserve - you get rewarded by their respect for you. Just give em a smile and an hola and hey u get a gr8 big cheery Dominican smile back I guaranteeJust have fun and make the most of this lovely island.

<Author>SHK1
<Content>Wonderful holiday, we can't wait to go back. We had one week in August at this resort, and like many others I was very concerned when I read some of the reviews on this site. I am glad to say my worries were completely unfounded. Rooms - We were in the village section and our room was fine, AC worked very well, bathroom was fine, beds a little hard. We had ants one morning but this turned out to be because my husband had spilt a sweet drink over his bag, and this seemed to have attracted them. We asked for someone to come and get rid of them and they did (we also cleaned the bag) and we never saw any more.Food- I was pleasantly suprised with the food, after the negative reviews I pictured sharing the table with a flock of birds at every meal but this was certainly not the case. There was the occasional bird, I think twice during our stay, and the staff did get rid of them. There was plenty of variety, and the standard of food was fine. We also ate at all three of the restaurants which were all nice, in particular the Japanese.Beach - The beach was gorgeous, the sand is lovely and cool, and the sea is nice and warm. It was all kept very clean.Pools - Very nice pools, these were also kept very clean. You did need to get there early if you wanted a bed with shade, but if you are a hard core sunbather and are not bothered about the shade then you will not struggle at any time of day to get a lounger.Heat!! - I completely under-estimated the heat, it was incredibly hot. I now know why most people go earlier in the year. Both my daughter and I got burnt on the beach on day one, quite badly as well, I ended up covered in blisters. This was despite factor 30 sun protection being applied regularly. Please be wanred, it is lovely playing in the sea (especially when all the fish swim around your feet), but it takes no time at all to burn, and you don't realise until it is too late. Staff - All the staff we dealt with were polite and helpful, and they work incredibly hard. I think people just look for things to complain about sometimes, I witnessed people being rude to the staff and then complaining to anyone who would listen, unfortunately I think these are the people that then go and place very negative reviews trying to put others off. Thankfully we were not put off and had a fabulous holiday as a reuslt.

<Author>Yher
<Content>Excellent hotel for what you pay for My husband and I had to fly to Punta Cana at the last minute and stayed at this hotel for 6 nights and it was great!!! I've stayed at those so called 5 star hotels in punta cana and believe me the 5 stars doesn't compare to this 4 star hotel. Last year we traveled with the kids and stayed at Iberostar Punta Cana, supposedly 5 star, and when I compared the two, IFA is much better. Food is much better at IFA even though I didn't make reservations to the a la carte, I enjoyed the buffet restaurants specially at La Casona that was next to my villa. When you visit another country you want to get out of the ordinary and eat typical dishes from that country. La Casona had Mangu every morning, at lunch and dinner they tried to mix typical dishes with other continental dishes and the desserts were great specially the Flan which was my favorite. I am usually a picky eater, but here I went aboard eating everything--I wish I can bring the Cook with me to NY!!! I didn't experience any slowness in the service for getting my drinks at these restaurants--on the other hand my husband was already wined out for so much wine he had.Rooms' air conditioner was good although the first day was leaking, but got fixed before the night was over. I had a few issues with the hair dryer, but got it repaired and also I was missing the cord on the phone, which also was resolved. The rooms were clean and I never saw bugs.The pools and beaches are beautiful. I am not too crazy about salty water, but here I stayed in for almost an entire day.. The water was warm, crystal waters, clean and most of all WARM. Not like the beaches here in the US that are always cold. Beautiful scenery and spectacular views.Shows and night life were also great! We went to the disco close to the beach almost every night and had a great time. Great gym and spa. Gym is bigger than most hotels and with more equipment.Overall my stay was excellent and is like another person mentioned -- IT IS WHAT YOU MAKE OF IT. Don't give an attitude if you don't want to get an attitude. :o)

<Author>Suky2
<Content>Worst vacation we have Ever taken-Don't Go! I have travelled many times to the Caribbean and Mexico and have never encountered such a bad resort. The service, food, and accommodations were beyond terrible. About a half hour after we arrived, I was literally in tears because I felt so bad for my boyfriend that I had screwed up and chosen this place. I wasn't expecting the 4 Seasons, but come on...Some specifics:1. Upon check-in, we were told our room wasn't ready. OK, no big deal. An employee (I guess?) grabbed my suitcase and started walking away with it. Luckily, I speak enough Spanish to get by, (because NO ONE from beginning to end spoke any English or even made an attempt to be polite when I tried to speak their language.) The employee who was walking away with my suitcase said it would be $5 US for him to watch my bag until our room was ready. (He knew enough English to ask for my money). What reputable resort charges money to watch your bags???? I took my suitcase and walked away.2. While waiting for our room, my boyfriend and I went to the buffet to have some lunch. After a few bites of some kind of rancid meat and chewy vegetable, the tears began. Now, I am not a picky eater by any means. I love to try new things and will eat almost any type of food. THIS WAS INEDIBLE. There were also birds and flies landing on the food all week and no one seemed to notice. I literally ate a roll with butter for dinner on 2 or 3 nights (and the roll was bad).3. Our room- Disgusting. Full-sized sheets on king bed didn't cover mattress. Bitten by ants/flies (?) and was scratching all week. Door to balcony was broken. Holes in towels. Stains on everything. Imagine sleeping on a brick with a scratchy, ripped sheet partially covering it.4. 7 restaurants (???) The web site we used boasted 7 places to eat. There are 2 identical buffets (inedible above), but what they don't tell you is that you need to make reservations at the 3 real restaurants, which are only open for dinner. We had to wait in a long line to speak to the 1 employee who takes these reservations, to be told there were none available for the first 3 nights of our trip. I had to get in line every morning before 9:00 am to get a crack at a spot for the next night. We had 2 semi-edible meals (Japanese and Caribbean) the entire trip. 5. Room not cleaned until almost dinnertime (if at all). No new towels on 2 days. Tile floor stayed sandy  dirty all week.6. Need to pay extra to use the (rusty) safety deposit box!!! Didn't feel our valuables were safe and heard of theft from a couple. We ended up leaving our TV on and putting on the Do Not Disturb sign when we left the room to ease my mind a little.7. After 24 hours my boyfriend asked me if we could call the airline and have our flight moved up so we could leave early. We would rather have eaten McDonald's  been at home.8. Met 1 couple from the US. Most people were European and seemed nasty and rude to Americans. The US couple spent over $100 per meal to eat dinner at a place reachable by boat down the beach. We thought about it but didn't want to waste any more $ on the worst trip of our lives.9. Got 1 bottled water each on first day in room fridge. Had to reuse empty bottle  fill with tap (?) water in dispensers at buffet.10. Bar- Apparently all-inclusive means a 6-ounce plastic cup with warm, flat Dominican beer. No other beers or even cans/ bottles. There was one brand of local rum that made my boyfriend sick ( he can drink). I saw someone get a white wine one night (I had been told there was no wine, even after being nice, speaking Spanish,  tipping). Now, I'm no wine snob, we have a box of wine in our friedge, but this was undrinkable. I threw it out after a sip. 11. Had the runs most of the week (see food above).12. Nothing to do at night (a cheesy show of some kind, all in Spanish, and a disco that was basically a buffet floor after 11 pm). Too dangerous to leave the resort.So...I wish I had been smart enough to read this site before making my decision. It was a stupid call. Never use Jetaway Holidays or go to Villas Bavaro Beach. Would I have gone to the trouble of writing all this if it wasn't that bad??????????

<Author>Dette100
<Content>It was lovely ! My friends and I stayed here from 1st - 15th May 2006. As it was a last minute booking, I was a bit apprehensive after reading the reviews on here. I had said to my friends that if it really was as bad as people said, I was going to change hotels !! We had abolsultely NO reason to do so, the place is really good. We arrived at the reception via taxi from Punta Cana airport (as we didn't want to wait for the coach with other drop off's before us, it only cost $25 for the 3 of us). We asked for a beach view room but were told that it was near to the disco and would be quite noisy at night - we didn't really believe them as we thought that they we just fobbing us off. Our rooms (we had 1 each) were in the village section and were fantastic, 1 had a view of the gardens and the other a view of the lake with ducks and other birds. They were very clean, with remote controlled tv, mini fridge (stocked daily with water) and a nice bathroom with plenty of towels provided. Our maid arrived around 9am each day, just when we were leaving for breakfast. One friend really didn't believe the guy on reception regarding the beach view rooms and opted to have one - glad I didn't !! We went back to her room one night for a night cap and the noise from the disco was really loud and made the patio window vibrate, nice and loud when we were in there mind ! but when I need sleep I like it to be quiet !The food was good in both the buffet restaurants but the one nearest the reception was the best. At breakfast there was an vast selction of food from toast and pastries to a separate grill chef cooking every which way with eggs. Lunch we either spent at the restaurant on the beach which served burgers, fries and chicken each day but we got a bit feb up with that as the week went on, then we started to get the shuttle bus (to hot and lazy for the 10min walk!) to go to the main restaurants. We went for dinner each evening at around 8pm and had no trouble at all getting a table. We tried the other restaurants too and they were also good, we usually booked them with customer services after breakfast about 2 days in advance and they had no trouble at all meeting our requests.The entertainment was not to my taste but the animation team did their best to arrange something for everyone. The disco was ok but they tended to play alot of salsa music but hey I'm on holiday!! They had numerous activities daily on the beach from dancing lessions, aqua aerobics to vollyball. Something for everyone (but try and get us girls off of our sunloungers).The beach was gorgeous, beautiful white sand and clear warm water, needless to say we spent all of our time there. The people were friendly and couldn't do enough for us, they always had a smile on their faces and made us feel very welcome. We made some great friends and had great times.There is only one thing I didn't like about this place and that was the photographers on the beach with animals, I wish people wouldn't let them take their pictures with them - but that is only my opinion.This place is well worth the price we paid, so much so, we are thinking about going again later this year. A holiday is what you make it, so relax and enjoy !!

<Author>Cadrezzate
<Content>We had a great family holiday We are an Irish Famly and we went on a wonderful holiday to the Dominican Republic April 9th to 24th 2006. We stayed at the IVA Villas, Bavaro Beach, Punta Cana and we were very happy with the village, accommodation, staff and proximity to the stunning beach. We enjoyed the holiday so much that we already want to go back next year. Our only complaint was that while booking this hotel we were told that there were tennis and basketball facilities and that all non-moterized sports were free with our package.My 3 children aged 18, 15 and 13 all love to play tennis. On our second day my children got into their tennis gear and got their racquets and were intending to go to the tennis court by themselves. I decided to go with them to watch them play and find out where the tennis courts were. Lucky I did! The so-called tennis courts were a 15 minute walk from the hotel. On the way we had to pass through a rough area where the builders were making comments to my daughters and when we finally found the courts they were on a totally abandoned piece of land in a dangerous-looking area with rubbish thrown around and the smell of urine. The courts were in a totally abandoned condition and I鈥檓 quite sure nobody had played tennis there for years. There was no sign of a Basketball courtMy children were very disappointed and so I went to complain and to ask if anything could be done as these facilities were specifically mentioned in the brochure. I spoke to my tour representative and she agreed with me that the facilities were bad but that they would be building new courts soon. I said that this was not good enough and that my children were expecting to play tennis every day and I asked if it would be possible to use the facilities at the next door hotel which was also used by our tour operator. She checked and said this was not possible. I then talked to the Hotel management who were equally unhelpful.We did not make a fuss as we were enjoying our holiday. We did try to use the windsurfers and the sailboats which were on our beach but were told that we had to pay for them. We could only use the canoes for free. As windsurfers and sailboats are non-motorized, according to the brochure they should have been free.For anyone travelling to this resort and wanting to use these facilities I suggest you check with your tour opeartor or the hotel directly to see if this situation has changed. The hotel should either take out all references to Tennis Courts, Basketball Courts and Free Non-Motorized Sport from thier brochure or provide these services using the facilities of a sister hotel until such time as new ones are built for the Ocean Village.I would like to stress however that we would go back to the same hotel, it was very good value for money, the facilities provided were clean and if you tipped the staff and practised your Spanish they were friendly. Just dont expect anything to be done in a hurry! We stayed in the villas closest to the stunning beach, which was very handy, but do not ask for these if you have trouble sleeping as the disco is nearby and very loud! We didnt mind this and our teenage girls were thrilled with the proximity of the evening entertainment. Security is very good there.We found the food to be good in general and quite good at the theme restaurants. We were careful with the drinking water and none of us got sick.If you fancy a tour outside the complex, contact Zereida at RH TOURS S.A in the town of Bavaro (Phone 552 1425). She is a lovely lady (she speaks perfect American) who will organise individual tours to where ever you want to go and was very helpful to us in finding our way by local bus to Santo Domingo City (a fab experience! try it)Be adventurous and travel outside the complex. We took the local busses, which cost nothing and are fun, the conductor travels along hanging out of the open doorway and the bus veers all over the road to avoid the potholes! (just like in Ireland!) He holds a huge wad of cash in his hand and shoves three or four into each double seat! That way you get to see the real people and of course the poverty, you need to be careful but we never felt threatened and our kids got an education. Most of the time we were the only white people on the bus. Santo Domingo the city is very run down but interesting, a bit like Havana in Cuba. Our busride there (4 hours) was fun if a bit hair-raising! they drive like lunatics! We saw tobacco fields, cocco plantations, cane sugar plantations and lovely colourful wooden houses along the way and stopped halfway at a roadside hut where everybody got off the bus for 20 minutes and had all sorts of fried stuff to eat! THE BEACH IS STUNNING! Go with a positive attitude and Enjoy it!

<Author>tiques4u
<Content>Fantastic ... We Can't Wait To Return ... Ex. Value for the $$$ Excellent value for the money spent. We just returned on Aug 13th 2006 from Punta Cana and the IFA Villas Bavaro resort. Our room (3608) was quite large with a king size bed, color TV w/remote, mini-fridge and a large balcony overlooking one of the 3 pools. The A/C was ice cold and the water pressure was always very good. They had a soap/shampoo/conditioner dispenser in the shower which was great and always full. Yes, you do need to bring your own washcloths (small inconvienence). Maid service was always prompt and we had no shortage of towels. The staff in general was first rate from the front desk and guest services to the many restaurants and bars they we enjoyed throughout the week. It was a short walk (7-8 mins) to the beach or you could take the shuttle bus if you wanted. The water was very clear and beautiful and the white sugar sand beaches just seemed to invite long walks. The food was fabulous at every meal. There were lots of choices and they were all very good. The seafood (Marlin, Snapper, Swordfish, Squid) was some of the best that I have ever eaten anywhere throughout the world. I could go on and on about the overall excellence of this resort and how special we were made to feel, but my advice to you is not to wait too long to visit or more people will have found out how great it is and the ratings will go up and the prices will surely follow. It is currently priced as a budget resort but it deserves a lot better. Don't let your travel agent talk you into spending more $$$ to upgrade your hotel. With the IFA Villas Bavaro it is not necessary. We can't wait to return and we hope that you have as great a vacation as we did. Maybe we will see there on our next trip. Kim  Milan from Canton, Ohio.

<Author>vascience_teacher
<Content>I would go back again. As others have stated, I was very paranoid about the IFA Villas Bavaro AFTER I booked the trip. It wasn't until then that I came across Tripadvisor and I read a number of negative reviews of the resort. I stayed at IFA between the dates of August 7-11. Here is my review of the trip:Check In Service:When we arrived, There were about 15 people waiting to be checked in but only one person doing the checking in. This was very annoying because they did not have a system so others were being helped out of turn. It took maybe 30 minutes before we received the key to our room.The Room:Upon entering the room, I was very disappointed. There was a dead dried up bug stuck to the wall (it looked as if it had been there all summer). The headboard was attached to the wall but there was a huge space between the board and the mattress. The mattresses themslves looked 20 years old! I Being a germaphobe, I was afraid to sleep on it ( I sprayed lysol all over the bed!) The bathroom looked old, the tubs need to be replaced asap. The one consistent tip that I read about this hotel is the lack of washclothes, they did not lie! It is as if they don't exist there. After I saw the room, I went back to the front desk and asked if i could be changed to a different section of the hotel ( the village) I was told that I would be unable to move for two days because the hotel was booked. It was worth the wait so I did. After the change I was VERY pleased. The new room actually looked like a nice hotel room. No scary bugs or rusted tubs, it was very nice.The Food:There are two buffets on the resort. It wasn't as bad as other reviews. The menu basically stayed they same, but you could always find something to eat. The Service:The service was great. Everyone was polite and nice.The Beach:BEAUTIFUL!! Just be careful when you go to the market. The vendors are VERY aggressive!Conclusion:For $700, this was a very nice trip. It included airfare, hotel, food, and alcohol. I would definately return to the IFA resort, but I will NEVER stay in the VIllas. Only the Village or Ocean Village.

<Author>CJGibel
<Content>Great Vacation! We stayed from 7/17/06-7/24/06. As many others have written we were apprehensive about going due to the bad reviews. There were 4 of us, 2 adults and 2 teenagers.First, Do Not take traveler checks. They are very hard to exchange. Also, if you use credit cards they charge you a fee. US dollars are accepted everywhere.Next, the food. We never went hungry and no one got sick. There was always plenty of food to choose from. Remember, their trying to please many different nationalities. However, in the buffet resturaunt near the beach, birds fly in since there is no netting to keep them out. We did see some on the food a few times, but the workers shooed them away. We thought the food was better at the front buffet resturaunt near the lobby. As for the specialty resturaunts , the Mexican was good but it's still served buffet style, early seating is a bad time, it's way to hot! The Japanese we had reservations for but heard that it was not very good so we ended up not going. The Caribe was okay, it is the only air conditioned one and you were served by the staff, they were very friendly. When you get your room number make your reservations for those resturaunts right away. Beware of the milk in the carfe's which they use for the coffee in the am, more than once they poured my coffee then the milk and it was spoiled. The room, We had to wait about 2 hrs for our room since our flight was early. I packed our swim suits and a couple of towels in our carry on, while we waited the kids went swimming. We were in the Villas, the room could have used a little upgrading but I think we spent at the most 1 1/2 hrs a day in the room other than when we slept. We left our maid $2 a day and she always made sure we had plenty of towels and water to brush our teeth with. Our ac always worked. When we arrived in our room there was a broken window in the bathroom. We told our Apple Rep and they fixed it the same day. Once we had no water for a few hours but we were leaving for the pool anyway so it really didn't matter. The water was back on by the time we were getting ready for dinner. It is quite a walk from the villas to the beach but they always had a shuttle bus running. The nightly shows are near the villas and there is a bar over the pool which is nice. Make sure you take wash cloths, they do not give you any.The staff, all in all everyone was pleasant enough, there were a few times when we had to wait at the reception area, it was somewhat disorganized. The most unpleasant person we encountered was the lady who takes the reservations for the resturaunts. The beach, Wonderful. It is beautiful. The only drawback is there are no umbrellas. Invest in one the attaches to the lounge chair and take it with you if you can. We went para-sailing, awesome!I 'd have to say our overall experience was good. We met some wonderful people from the UK and plan to go again next year with them. Remember, it's what you make of it. If you want to find something wrong you will.

<Content>Great Vacation This vacation was a pleasant surprise. After reading the reviews prior to us leaving for this vacation I was a bit apprehensive/nervous. Would I go back? Certainly, for the same price.

<Content>Above average scenery, accomodations...Below average service Wife  I went 7/17/06-7/21/06 on a good ole' vacation. We are from South Carolina. Beach and blue ocean water are breathtaking. We parasailed and rented little speedboats and drove to a snorkeling pool. Very pleased with water sports. Food was what we expected and we even thought it was a little better than the 5 star resort where we honeymooned 2 years ago. Lodging was a little weak. It reminded us of a mountain chalet with the very high ceilings. Our view was of scaffolds, as the were doing something to the brick wall outside our room. But that was no real bother, we knew we got a deal on this trip and that everyting would not be perfect. My problem was with the service. There are 3 nice restaurants in this resort. We were told we just had to make reservations a day or so in advance. So we decided to be smart and book all at once on the first day...we BARELY got in one of them, never getting to eat in the other two. Said they were just too packed. The little girl working the Guest Services table was down right rude and I finally had to tell her that she should be more personable. Bartenders and waitresses had this weird little attitude that I think had a little bit of LAZY in it. Many times had to ask over and over for a sprite with dinner. Bartenders took their sweet time coming over to get drink order at pool bar and Captain's Bar. They were busy singing and dancing and basically being Joe Cool with each other and other guests that seemed of Latin decent...wouldn't make eye contact, acted like they couldn't understand me in English or Spanish (and my basic Spanish isn't bad at all) just what I consider very uncool. Especially considering that we are paying pretty decent $$$ for this trip!!! Had this uneasy feeling that Americanos were last on the list, so to speak. Spoke with others that rode the bus back to the airport with us that got the same vibe. It was weird. We have always done our tropical vacations in Mexico where you are generally made to feel very welcome and that is why I will spend my money there in the future. Would not recommend DR unless you are just ultra bored with your usual vacation spots. This was resort was considered 3 stars and I didn't realize that pertained to service, as well. Maybe it would be different at a nicer place in the DR???

<Author>sohnstad
<Content>Stay away from this place! I'm not one to slam a hotel or resort that I have been to, but this was the worst! I realy want to warn you. No airconditioning, or at least none that worked. We only had the fan on the ceiling that was wobbling and thought it might fall to the floor! We even had no water for half a day. There was some problem. We talked to a couple from Pennsylvania, New Jersey, and Kentucky and we all told each other of airconditioning problems and other things so we were far from alone by feeling this way. We all also felt like we were discriminated against for being Americans. None of us will be back here. I dont want to knock DR. the beaches are wonderfull and the water nice and warm. We just picked a awful hotel! Sometimes saving a buck realy isnt worth it! As far as all inclusive, ya, if you can get it out of them. We waited several times at the Captins bar to be waited on, once you make eye contact with the waitress, she turns around like she never saw you. My husband and I made a game out of it and gave her a dollar tip everytime she would finaly wait on us, (and there wasnt hardly anyone there) She would come and take our empty glasses and walk away without asking if we wanted anything else. At lunch and dinner, if you wanted a coke or sprite or house wine you had to specificly ask for it, they would never offer the choice, they only wanted to give you water. Water in your rooms was scarce too. They are supposed to supply you with 2 bottles of water a day in your refridgerator and we got only 3 total for the the 5 nights we were there. Oh, and dont bring any US dollars over 10.00 cuz they hate to give you change. Even the loby refused to make change for us from a 20.00 bill. So, if you do choose this place bring lots of 5.00 and 1.00's and maybe some 10.00's. The pools were nice. I only used the one near the villas and theater. We saw one good show put on and the rest were ok. The beach is beautiful and the food at the beach was by far the best. The buffets were ok, we found it hard to find something that we liked, but everyone has different taste. I went to the Mexican resturant and it was ok, but not what I would have expected. When I walked in there it was like an oven, hotter in there than outside! had choice of rices, salads and chicken tacos, fajitias and quesidias which by the way were all made the same, so who could tell! Very hard to get reservations. They wanted to give me 9pm reservations at one resturant, does any body realy eat that late?? Not me. Guess I should have held out some US dollars to get something decent cuz we found that by tipping at the buffets and the bars, you will get waited on and not ignored. We went snorkeling one day, it was a blast. On the Kontiki party boat. They picked us up from our hotel and spend a good part of the day snorkeling, drinking, dancing. We also went to the Maniti Park, it was ok, it was a day away from our hotel! I swam with the dolphins. They picked you up at your hotel too, on this open sided bus with music, the ride was fun too.Oh,one more thing, we had some little ants in our room which we could have lived with, until they started bitting the heck out of our bodies. We wouldnt know they were there till we felt a pinch then we found them and killed them. I just hope I didnt bring too many home in my luggage. That's all we'd need!

<Author>Travelbug002
<Content>IFA: (Incredibly False Advertisement) We thought we got a good deal when we got an All Inclusive package to this resort and only paid $545 per/person for 5days/4 nights. The package included, food  drinks, airfare, tips and taxes but what they forgot to include was CUSTOMER SERVICE, but thats just the start of it all.Food  Drinks? The food was edible if you dont mind flies and crows flying all over your plate and all over the buffet table. Drinks? If your lucky enough to get someone to come over to you or even acknowledge your presence, please be sure to order 3-4 drinks at a time, because you will be waiting 20-30 minutes between each drink. The swim up bar? It has a bar, but no liquor and no bartender. You can probably get can drink in the desert easier than you would at this resort.Rooms? The couple rooms (the rooms with the King size beds, fyi: #'s start with 10) are on the other side of the resort. The walk from your room to the beach was about 10- 15 minute walk in 100 degree weather. But the room itself, it was in OK condition, not impressive at all. The sheets dont get changed, the towel wrack (in our bathroom) was hangin off the wall, but then again maintence does not leave you any wash cloths (so pack your own!). If you do happen to go to IFA, before you settle in make sure your Air Conditioning is working. Two of our friends did NOT have A/C for 2 nights, complained to Front desk (for 2 full days) but got no service. It wasnt until they threatened to leave that there room was changed. The bottled water in the fridge is not new, they refill the bottles (with God only hope filtered water) but I highly doubt it since most of us got sick.Secuirty of your goods? Renting the safe ($3 a day), is definitely worth the money here. How is that of one of our friends lost his Ipod and phone charger, after he had the Do Not Disturb sign at the door the whole time we were there? Reservations at the Caribbean, Japenese  Mexican restaurant? In one word? Impossible. We tried to make reservations the day we got there and they were all booked. How do you offer a service and then not give everyone a fair chance at it.All in all, we would have been willing to over look, all these details, if the Customer Service was even close to decent, we did only pay $525 per person. However, maybe we are wrong, but we still expected some kind of customer service. If somebody would had even showed a sign that they cared, maybe our experience would have been at least average. But the bottom line is that anyone that we dealt with, treated us like we were bothering them and that they simply did not care. So in my opnion, save your money and go somewhere else, because the highlight of our trip was coming home.

<Author>AMeyer
<Content>OK but pay the extra for a better hotel My boyfriend and I stayed at the IFA for one week 13th July - 21st July. I am glad it was only a week as it did become a bit boring eating the same food and the entertainment was poor - v cheesy! We stayed in the Ocean section which did look a lot nicer than the villas section. The rooms were ok, but the bath was past its best and the fridge had rust marks which does not give a good first impression. The bed was comfy and the air con worked fine. No bugs in the room, just a small lizzard which my boyfriend said if i catch he would give me 拢20 (I caught it and I'm still waiting for the payout!)The pool by the villas is better. The pool by the ocean block looked like it needed a good clean. Someone stole our hotel beach towel so be warned or you will have to pay the $20 for each towel. The water aerobics was good fun.The staff are very slow and don't seem to comprehend the concept of next in the queue as many times I was next but the bar staff proceeded to serve another guest! Getting a drink in the buffet restaurant was hard work! So slow, so by the time you finished your meal, the drink stil hadn't arrived. We tried to book for the Japanese but it was full Book any reservations for the restaurants on your first day or you won't get in for the duration of your stay. We tried to book the Japanese after the lady doing the reservations made a mistake with the restaurant we wanted, but she refused to amend our booking to the Japanese, saying it was full and there was nothing she could do! V unhelpful.We didn't get upset stomachs, which was surprising as there were so many flies and birds on the food. The staff did not attempt to shoo away the birds. The buffets were surprisingly ok, but the same food day in and day out did become tedious. The pasta chef was good and it was nice to see something fresh cooked in front of you. I wore insect repellant and only got one bite. My boyfriend did not bother with the spray and did not get any! The table tennis ball was broken from the day we got there unitl the day we left, and the staff had no interest in replacing it. The grounds were lovely and the beach was nice too, although we stayed mostly at the pool as there were no parasols on the beach. They keep the public toliets execptionally clean and fresh smelling.All in all, it was good value for money but i recommend spending the extra and going for a 5* resort.

<Author>AdamHanna
<Content>Good resort. Great Beach. Great Holiday. (It's what you make it!) We stayed for 2 weeks at IFA and we had a ball. My wife and I brought my wife's younger brother and sister with us. We stayed in the Villas and I was apprehensive having read some bad reviews of the vills. We stayed in 1139 at the villas and were well up at the back of the complex. It suited us fine as our nearest pool was the best pool in the complex with the margarita bar over it, and the el-captain bar beside it. The island itself is pretty big and the population generally live in poverty. Holiday resorts are first world pockets in a third world country. They are a proud and clean people though. I timed the walk from the beach to our villa and it was 8 minutes at a leisurly pace. There is a little bus that drives you around the complex but the walk is very pleasant through well tended gardens and absolutley safe.  Security is strong throughout the resorts in the Dominican Republic. We saw a security guard on the beach late one night who was armed. One night I couldn't sleep as a large electrical storm swept through and I watched the guards walk aropund the complex all night. I felt assured of my safety but concerned that the need for that security existed.  THE STAFF. Generally very pleasant. As this was a spanish speaking Island, I tried to learn some phrases which appeared to be appreciated by the staff. We left a dollar tip for our maid every day which is a good idea. Our room was generally sorted by mid afternoon and when we needed towels we got them. The reception staff seemed to be stressed at times, particularly when a large group of people were checking in or out. Customer service was very good and from here we booked our resteraunts (discussed Later). THE ROOM. The room was large and airy. Nice big variable speed fan in the centre of the room and great airconditioning. Ours was leaking badly when we arrived but within ten minutes a maintenance man had fixed the problem. TV is ok, a few channels we could understand but I didn't go to watch TV. Working fridge in the rooms. If you buy water anywhere, keep your bottles and fill them up at night from the bars or resteraunts. DO NOT use the tap water for brushing your teeth. Don't even let the shower water get in your mouth. We were very strict about this and none of us was sick. Bathrooms in the villa's could do with a big make over but again I'm not spending my holiday time in the bathroom (Hopefully)! Very few bugs. In our 2 week stay we had one cockroach in the bathroom which was easily dealt with. Don't leave your door open or to long as there are oportunist frogs and geckos, again easy dealt with. Throw a sheet over them and take them back out. No ants in the room but we kept the food in the rrom in the fridge.  THE FOOD. The food was alright. You could always find something to eat. They could vary the food a bit more but I always ate well. Service can be a little slow but there are so many people eating these buffets it must be hard to keep up.  We tried the Japanese resteraunt, It was alright. Wouldn't have gone back to it. We tried the Mexican resteraunt, it was alright. Wouldn't have gone back to it.  We didn't get to try the carribean resteraunt unfortunatley.Try them for yourself. If you don't like them go to the buffet and eat instead.  Watch the drinks, they are very generous and not watered down. It can sneak up on you and it's not to pleasant in that heat! THE BEACH Wow! Fantastic! Lovely palm tree beach. We walked up and down the beach past several other resorts and ours was by far the cleanest. Staff are out every morning lefting in the seaweed brought in. The resort staff try the best at entertaining on the beach through the day but if it's not your scene there is loads to do anyway. There are markets (discussed later). fishing tours, parascending, speedboats, a massive water slide, the list goes on and on. Bring your sun cream with you. It's very dear to buy and we used a lot of it. You can get burnt very easily on the beach without realising. Be aware that there are a lot of topless women at this resort beach and pool. THE POOL. We loved our pool at the villa's. Seemed to be the largest, deepest and often the most quiet. Went through quite a lot of inflatable balls as the shrubs around the pool are all thorny. At 7am the staff are out washing down the pool area and all the sunloungers which were all in working order. We had some money stole on our last day there. We suspect it was taken from our bag when we at the pool. Thankfully it wasn't much and at the end of our trip but it was very annoying. At this pool is the stage area for the evening entertainment. THE ENTERTAINMENT. Not the best but the do try very hard. Bingo is not my cup of tea! Lots of dancing extravaganzas and a stand up show once a week. The stand up show was simple, funny and somewhat adult orientated.  THE REPS. They are all around the reception area in the mornings. Our Rep was pleasant enough and contactable 24hrs a day but not very impressed when he knew we had bought excusions from another rep. He spoke his mind I respect that in a person but i also know he was annoyed because he lost out on the deal. Shop around and get the best deal. The two reps that we would recommend are Felix from MyTravel and Emmanuel from HotelBeds. Best to make you own mind up. THE BEACH MARKETS. These are good craic if you fancy haggling! Everybody is your friend, you can feel the love in this place (for your money)! These guys are kings at haggling and they know how to rip you off big time. If they make you an offer, counter it with at least half the price. They will haggle but stick to your guns. If they won't give in tell them you will look around and maybe call back later. They usually call you back and give in to your price. The guys selling rum will often share a drink with you to get in your good books. Fun but you can get cheap rum on some of the excusions. The jewelry is probably fake. They will give you a free necklace but we took them off a soon as we could because it probaly told the other market sellers that we were mugs! Go forth and Haggle! THE EXCURSIONS. We did a lot of excursions. We booked the speedboats on the beach. Four of got into a speed boat and our guides took another speed boat. We raked about in the sea which was great fun and they tied the boats up at a bouy and we snorkelled. The little sister was pretty scared but the guide held her hand throughout and the fish were just amazing. They would eat bread straight out of your hands! We went horseback riding for two hours (required six hours resting in pool before sitting down again!), at the ELPat Ranch. I thought my horse looked like it was about to die and we didn't really see eye to eye, so they gave me another one. We had a much better understanding, it went were it wanted and I hung on! Good fun but the hour riding would have been enough. We went on the dune buggy adventure which was great fun. Bring spare clothes with you cos you do get muddy. We stopped at a Dominican farm and drunk their coffee (Fantastic). The excursion lasted half a day but do be careful on the roads. There was an Italian couple who loved to swerve about despite being told not to by the guides. They very, very nearly swerved out infront of a bus that was overtaking them. The bus drivers reaction saved them.  We went to Saona Island which was to be an amazing desert island experience. It was a two hour coach ride stopping at a nice place where Apocolypse Now and Rambo II were filmed. then we got speed boats out to the island stopping a pools in the sea where it was waist deep and you could swim. On to the island which was abig let down. It was comercialised and tacky. We got a catamaran on the wasy back and as the sun was out we sat on the netting at the front to do some sun bathing. Nice...... Until the tropical storm hit us! The rain came down sideways and there was lighning around us. Being on a metal boat in the sea with lighting is not my idea of heaven. We all were shivering with the cold when we got back to the bus for our two hour journey home. Didn't like that excursion.  Deep sea fishing was an experience. We went about 11 miles out and i was so glad we took anti sickness tablets before we left cos once we got out past the reef it was 9 foot swells all the way. Four hours of being bobbed up and down, watching some others be violently ill over the side and we didn't catch a thing (well, 1 fish caught by an american who grabbed the rod every time something took a bite and didn't understand the concept of sharing!). Best excursion we did was called the Jurassic Safari. It was fantastic. I learnt more about the Domincan People and life in that one day than I learnt in the whole 2 weeks. They are a charity helping to raise money for the schools and some of the local families. These families allow you to see how they live as part of the trip. We drove up into the mountains and got on hoses again which were much healthier than the first. The forse riding is optional and lasts about 25 mins. On up into the mountains to their safari park and river where you can swim. Big buffet lunch and back down to see a 'safe' demonstration of the second most popular national sport....Cock fighting. (Didn't like that bit but I respect their culture and ways). We bought cheap rum on the way back home. $9 a bottle for 151 proof rum. Our guide was called Monchy and was very informative an entertaining. He workd 12 hour days, 24 in a row to get 6 days off!Did I enjoy my holiday? Absolutley. A holiday is what you make it. I listened to people who hated their trip and I felt that they would be hard people to please generally. If you want to moan you can always find something to moan about. If you want to have fun, it's there to be had!Would I go back? No, not to the Dominican Republic because I like to see different places and cultures. Not because I didn't like the island or the resort.Would I stay at an IFA resort again? Yes I would. Go Have fun and make up your own mind. Remember people love to complain but don't like to praise. A little praise goes a long way and is much more pleasurable.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Had a great time despite the flaws! Never having stayed in an all-inclusive resort, I didn't know what to expect. Having read the very mixed reviews for this hotel, I was nervous about our trip to this hotel.The reviews that I read were very accurate and helpful, so if you need information, read them. My family of 5 was placed in two rooms in the Villas section(1095, 1089) of the resort which I was not thrilled about after reading some of the reviews, but we were told that the other sections of the hotel were booked and we would have to come back in order to change rooms.(I did end up checking out a room in the middle of the resort on Tuesday, it was nicer, but by then my family had settled into our rooms and was happy with them.) The room itself was adequate but needed work. A new tub/shower unit, mattresses/bed frame, and pillows(which we later referred to as the cotton ball pillows) would make quite a difference in the room. Otherwise it was very clean. Our A/C worked infrequently but was adequate, in my husband's room his A/C worked great. The Villas are very cute. Each 1story building had 10 rooms in it. The rooms have a front porch with chairs. The pathway to the Villas, I felt, gave the place some charm. The grounds were well groomed and had beautiful trees and plants everywhere. The pool by the Villas was the best of the three pools. It was the deepest and had a bar in it. The Villas were also close to the 3 a-la-carte restaurants which you should try each at least once(*You must reserve in advance, so do it your first day there!). They are also close to the nightly shows that are put on by the very busy animation team.  The food at the buffets was good. Our favorite meal was breakfast because you could have an omelette made to order. At the buffets there was always plenty to choose from, however, the food was repeated, but plentiful, how could you complain?! You could be as busy as you liked or as relaxed as you wanted to be. There were many activities offered daliy. The beach is gorgeous!!! There is plenty to do. We snorkeled, borrowing the equipment for one hour and leaving a deposit of $30 per person. We saw some fish and plants near the back part of the roped in swimming area. We didn't use the other equipment available. We went on the 1/2 day excursion to the Marinarium which involved snorkeling with nurse sharks and rays. It was very nice. *Bring plenty of sunscreen; we went through a bottle by mid-week. *Do not drink or brush your teeth with the tap water. There is filtered water available at the bars and restuarants to drink. The room refridgerator had 2 bottles of water in it, also which you can ask to have replaced. *Bring Imodium and tums for stomach/digestion issues. *If you like to snack between meals, bring your own, a can of Pringle chips cost $4 at the hotel store. *Learn some Spanish, bring a dictionary, and at least try to speak their language. It makes things a lot easier. *Some women are topless at the pools and on the beach(more so here), so if this kind of thing makes you uncomfortable, be aware.****Have fun, relax, and forget about the little things; enjoy your vacation!!!!! If you book with Apple Vacations read on.... After booking our trip a few months in advance the price of the trip came down as the trip date approached. We had been asked to purchase the ADVOC insurance at $70.00 per person($350 for my family) so we didn't purchase it because we felt that it was too costly with very little return value. We were mistaken because we did not realize that the discounted price only worked when you purchased insurance. Just F.Y.I if needed.

<Author>jadeyl
<Content>ok The Ifa Villas is made up of 3 hotels, all in one 'complex' using the same facilities. what it doesnt tell you in the brochures is that it is in the middle of a private residential area, so when you enter the main gates dont be suprised to see lots of houses all multi coloured. Check-in was slow as the people at reception hardly spoke english. When we did get our key, we were taken to our room which was 4133 near to the beach. It was a lovely room with a king size bed and nice view. we were lucky as others had a view of some buliding work going on- not major, just building a wall round the complex. we had not 1 bug or lizard in our room, nor any problems with the air con. The only thing was that the patio door did not lock, which is a bit worrying as you could climb from the main staircase onto our balcony. We were a 2 minute walk from the beach, which was absolutly fantastic. The waters were warm and fish swam right up the shore all multi-coloured and different shapes. Brilliant for snorkelling. The walk to the beach is not bad as some people make out. Yes you walk down a path, but its nice and you can find all the cocunuts on the floor. The food- Well the buffet was suprisingly really good. There were different things nearly every night, and the was a pasta dish chef, kebab/mussels/burgers chef. On a morning there was on omlet chef and a girl that made fresh milkshakes, like pineapple and melon. The waiters were VERY slow, if you asked them for a drink, you would not get it unless you kept on asking. There was a young man who was very quick so we gave him a tip and he looked after us from then on.The mexican restaurnat was fantastic. NOT spicy unless you choose spicy things.The japonise was nice- the teriaki chicken was gorgeous.The caribbean was the best. The steak was to die for. The room was air-conditioned and really nice. Well worth waiting for as you have to book theses restauants in advance and they do book up quick. There was not a lot of entertainment unless you like everything in foreign.no-one spoke good english, and so on a night we were drawn to the ping pong table in the old gym. But someone smashed the ball, and when we kept on asking for a new one, we kept getting the reply- on vancation!Not many english there at all, we were a bit shocked and dissapointed at first. Not a lot to do for kids, other than swim in the pools and use the internet.We did 2 trips, quad biking and catalina island. Quad BIking was good. They took us to a gorgeous beach with green and blue waters, but the Catalina Island was absolutly fantastic and definetly worth visiting. You book it on the beach were you get the banana boat etc, and its 85 dollars pp. leave at 7, 2hr bus journey to the boat, then 20mins to the island. They let you snorkell in the sea off the island, and it was fantastic, the reefs were amazing. Then you go onto the isalnd and can sunbathe, snorkell again, or shop at the shops.they provide a buffet luch and you are on the island for about 3hrs. The island is a protected nature reserve and so no-one lives on the island.Overall we are glad we went to the ifa villas but we were very bored by the end of the 2 weeks. we would go back to the dominican but not this hotel.

<Content>I won't go back ! The food was terrible ! They probably serve better food in Guantanimo Prison. Birds sat on the food trays on the buffet and the waiters never even tried to shoo them away .The meat was unchewable, breads were moldy. We all got sick stomachs. When we tried to make reservations at the other restaurants, we were told they were booked. but when we walked by them later, we looked inside and they had many empty tables. So we were relegated to eat with the birds at the two buffets all week. We were lucky enough to get a newer building(3700). They stuck most of the other Americans in the 1000 buildings, far away from the beach. They had many complaints about thier rooms, leaking toilets, water stopping mid shower, bugs, etc... The beach.... well , for one, the resort is not directly on the beach. you have to walk a sandy path or take a shuttle from the lobby. It had boats moored everywhere, and the water smelled of diesel fuel.and there were no sun shades on the beach. The pools were so-so , and if you were lucky enough to get a chaise lounge, you had to watch out for the Frenchies from tossing your towels and bags on the ground and stealing your chairs. Thats another thing all together, they are rude, crude, and you grow tired of them so fast. If the Dominican Republic wants American tourists, it needs to become more American friendly. Maybe a start would be to place more reps in the resorts, and Airports that speak English. We won't be back to Punta Cana. This was our third trip to Punta Cana , and our third different resort. They all seem to be the same.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A great resort, depending on what you want... My boyfriend and I, both 30 and professional, were seeking a quiet, romantic, beach paradise vacation to relax. We booked through Apple Vacations, and didn't have any problems with their services. I decided that we may want to do all inclusive to make things easier. We were not really happy being so stuck with the way things work with an all inclusive package, but some people may really like it. We realized afterwards how much more we would have liked to eat where we wanted or go where we wanted without having to pay extra for very expensive excursions or wait in long lines to make dinner reservations at one of the hotel's three restaurants. IFA has a large buffet (food isn't the greatest, but we always found something to eat) and they have 3 restaurants you have to make reservations to eat in usually 4 nights in advance! If you can, try to get as many nights as possible in the Carribean Restaurant-they have an amazing filet (Japanese and Mexican were so-so but better than the buffet). Regardless, we had never heard of Punta Cana before researching it on the internet and it looked beautiful from pictures. It is beautiful with blue green water, but some beaches were more beautiful and well-kept than others (we actually went to the beach next to us several mornings b/c it was nicer and bigger). Off the beach resorts, the local area is very poor and sad to see, especially when we come in with so much money compared. One thing that pleasantly surprised us was the grounds of the IFA hotel. It is a really beautiful place with 3 beautiful pools and a lot of trees/plant life. We had the chance to see another hotel next door (a 5 star) and yes, it was a bit nicer in areas, but we didn't really see much difference except price. There are people from all over the globe (German, French, Puerto Rican) staying at IFA and most workers spoke only Spanish. We brought our dictionary and that helped a ton to communicate with the staff. The nightly entertainment is not something to write home about. The staff tried hard and they are a very friendly group of young adults putting out a great deal of effort to entertain a large, diverse audience. 2 nights of that was enough for us. Also, very important at least during the time of season we went (mid June), bring bugspray!! We got many bites even with bugspay. Also, bring anything you may need. I needed glide dental floss b/c I got something stuck in my tooth (and only brought the cheap kind with me) and it was $12 US dollars!! Whoa! Also, know that the beaches and pool areas have many topless women of all ages and sizes, so if you are bringing little kids, make sure both you and them are aware (especially the American travelers!) All in all, we had a nice time, the weather was beautiful, and with 50 sunblock, we didn't burn, but got a great tan!  
<Date>Jun 27, 2006

<Author>stepstephenson
<Content>For budget travelers only.... This resort is definitely for the budget traveler. Very few activitiies included in the all-inclusive. Yes, snorkeling is available free of charge but you can only snorkel in the roped off swimming areas. Free non-motorized sports activities...not sure what those were?!?! The one paddle boat at the resort looked like it had been stuck in the sand since the resort was built. Everything you do, you have to pay extra for unless you just prefer to lie on the beach or stay at the pool. Guests are told not to use the pool or beach after 7:30 because of heath risks. The resort adds chlorine to the water after that time. No game room or games to play except for Bocce ball. No darts, pool tables, or shuffle boards. As far as the food, my best advice would be to take plenty of your favorite snacks. My husband and I are not picky eaters but we struggled to find something appetizing every day. I was craving McDonalds by the time we left...didn't think I would ever say that lol. You pretty much have to plan your activities around the times food is served and there are no snacks. There are basically three main places to eat other than the a'la cart restaurants...the two buffets and the grill at the beach. One of the two buffets does not open for lunch and both buffet restaurants serve the same food so if you don't like what is served at one, it will do no good to walk to the other restaurant. The menus vary each day but very little. I survived mostly off of salads and bread. Both buffets have great breakfast. I had read that you had to stand in line to make reservations for the a'la cart restaurants. Not true...go to guest services in the lobby at any time and schedule all three at once. We ate at the mexican and Japanese. The mexican was not edible to us but the Japanese was good. We looked at the menu for the international and decided against making reservations. You cannot find anything to eat at the resort between 3:30 and 6, or after about 10. I didn't particularly care for the grill food at the beach but they have pretty good fries if they are hot. A lot of pork and beef were served but both were tough. Both my husband and I had mild stomach upset on and off all week. Be sure to take Pepto Bismol tablets. I read that advice before I left, and it really helped me. My husband, on the other hand, was determined to tough it out and he had a much harder time. We booked our travel through Vacation Express and wasn't given the option to book excursions at time of booking. We went snorkeling by the reef one day but we purchased that on the beach. The trip was much cheaper than what was offered by our tour rep. I would definitely recommend shopping around when you get to the resort. Be sure to take plenty of cash. Most places do not take credit cards and the ones that do tack on a hefty surcharge.When we booked our trip, we were mislead by the fact that there were three resorts. There are three AREAS of the one resort. We stayed in the Ocean Village section which was pretty close to the beach (within five mins.) This is not very far but after a few days you will get tired of the walk. The resort is very large so a good bit of walking is involved. The villas are much further away and you will have to take a trolley to get to the beach. They was some construction on a new spa/weight room near our room. It should be finished by the time you go as they were almost finished last week. There was no construction noise but we were awakened every morning by a large dog barking. I guess the dog was across the street from the resort. The annoyance was very small though.As far as bugs in the rooms, we did find one small roach but he probably came in from the outside or the hallway. There is a small gap beneath the door that he could have come through. The rooms were nice but not swept which is kinda gross if you walk bare-footed in the room. The floors of the room are tile which is nice but do need to be swept. If you do not speak spanish, I recommend taking a English/Spanish language conversion book because we had a very hard time communicating with staff in general. Very little English is spoken and it is frustrating for both parties. The resort will give you a towel card upon arrival. Be sure to guard your towels because you have to return the towels to get back your cards. If you don't, there is a $20 charge. We left ours in our bathroom one day and after housekeeping came, one disappeared. The beach towels are blue so could not have been taken by mistake. We reported it but the gentleman I spoke with insisted it must have blown away. He did not understand that the towels were in the bathroom, not balcony. He said it would be handled but nothing was ever done. We luckily found an extra by the pool. Also, room towels were picked up early in the morning and they were not brought back until late in the afternoon so you may want to bring extras or use your beach towels. You only get one towel and one hand towel per person. One morning, housekeeping took ours and my husband told the maid we needed them to shower. She said more in five minutes. We got them around 6 that night. You may want to try to iron your clothes before you go if possible. Irons are available but must be limited. We had to request one three times before it was delivered. We were told we could only use it one hour so I busted my butt trying to finish ironing everything so I would not have to request the iron again. The iron was still in the room six hours later. There are very few people there from the U.S. and most do not speak English. I was actually surprised by the overall rudeness in general from others. I thought it was just us, but I have noticed others on this forum complaining as well. For example, if a large group was walking down the sidewalk, they would not move to one side. This happened repeatedly. Also, we were looked over several times by the bartenders that would wait on people that were tipping heavily. We noticed frustration from other people waiting for drinks as well and some would just walk off. This is supposed to be all-inclusive and the bar is the only area to get any kind of drinks including soft drinks. I think tipping is important but not EVERY time you go to the bar. Also, the last morning we were there, there was a line at the omelet station and we had been waiting patiently and a lady walked right up to the front of the line and skipped everyone. The chef proceeded to take her order without even noticing what she had done. By that point I had reached boiling point and told him she was supposed to be a the END of the line. She did not even acknowledge the fact of what she had done. The main pool is busy with kids. There is no supervision. We saw young kids climbing up the rocks in the center of the pool and pushing each other and jumping off. We kept thinking that was an accident and lawsuit waiting to happen. We saw kids playing with emergency life preservers and wondered, Where are the parents? Later, we saw the parents playing on them. Go figure?!?! One day we saw two kids approximately 10 years old fighting in the pool. One had another in a head-lock and was pounding his face with his fist. Resort guests had to break them up...not sure where the parents were. Also, I hope you don't mind women topless. This was at all the pools and the beach. I would not feel comfortable taking my kids there. But then again, that's my personal preference....it may not bother others. Overall, we would not go back to this resort. The grounds and beach are beautiful but I would think you could get that from most resorts in Punta Cana.  
<Date>Jun 22, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Had a great time!!!!! This resort was great for the money. The pools were great and the beach was amazing. People complain about the walk to the beach but it's really not that bad. You have to be real lazy and picky to complain about the walk. Do take advantage of the excursions offered at the lobby of the hotel (we got great deals..look for patricia). We swam with the dolphins..(not at manati park) at dolphin island and thats in the ocean not a pool. We also did the carribean festival. you get snorkle by the coral reef,swim with nurse sharks and sting rays.  The food was also good. We felt that the buffet was the best because we had more options. We ate at the mexican once and at the caribe once. They were both O.K. but not a big deal. It seemed almost impossible to get a reservation at the caribe because everyone thought it was the best,however,we thought it was all a hype. Not a big deal. So if you miss the chance to get a reservation there don't stress. You won't be missing out on much. The room was also good. we didn't get a king size bed but that was because they didn't have any available when we got there. They offered to change our room the next day as soon as one became available but we choose to stay in the the double bed room. it was close to the pool and the food..lol  Overall we had an amazing time and would recomend the resort and the trip to anyone.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not A Bad Deal For The Price Overall not a bad resort. Having read all of the other ratings before we went, I must say most had some merit. As with any trip, and or place you can find good or bad, its all what you make of things that count. With that out of the way here's our view; not a bad resort for the price, but still only just good, 3 star, by Canadian standards.Lots of food, drink, clean, friendly staff etc etc. We would not mind telling others to go there, but if you do, make sure you stay in the villas, by the main pool best, we stayed in the ocean villas, and had a very nice room, king bed, super clean. Stay away from the rooms, they are in an older part of the resort, and are a bit run down, not to mention, way out of the way, far from the bars, pool, and beach.What else to say, well the beach venders, are aggressive, and this island is not a place to wonder off by yourselfs, but you are safe, if you stay in the normal, areas, and shopping centres, as recomended by your tour reps. Nice beaches, some great tours, and lots of sun and sand. We would go back to Punta Cana again, but would pick another resort, and spend more money. Again it was welll worth what we paid,and it was one of the nicest trips. Having been to many islands ie Grand Cayman, Cuba , etc, this island is a good buy for the money, and a lot of fun. So with that all said, enjoy your vacation there, don;t sweat the little things and enjoy yourselfs, lifes too short not too.PL

<Author>Hurlbut
<Content>Try a week and see what you think We just spent 2 weeks at this hotel. This was our first time to this hotel but our 6th time to the Dominican. Needless to say, we were not expecting 5 stars like in the big USA cities. I felt that the rooms were average Dominican rooms- needed some updating, but safe and secure. They put bottled water in your room fridg and you can refill them at the bar. At most other resorts we have been at the room fridg had beer and soda. You have to rent the room safe that is located in the closet- for 2 weeks it was around 26 US dollars. There are no face cloths so bring your own. They do have hair dryers to use in the room. There is a nice balcony for each room. Towels are given out each day for pool use- you just have to present your towel card at the booth and you will get new towels. The room was in the 4000 block building and our friends were in the 3000 block-this actually turned out to be a good spot. The Villas are on the other side of the hotel that can be divided into 3 sections. If you are in the villas section, you will have a little walk to the beach or can catch the Beach Bus that travels constantly back and forth. The 3000 and 4000 block is in between the first noisy, younger people, party crowd pool and the quieter, older but fun second pool. There is a very nice pool in the Villas section (probably the nicest one). There are bars in each section. The service is very slow at the bars unless you make quick friends with one of the staff members - tip well. Doris was wonderful at the Lobby Bar near the second quieter pool. The food was average-not great-not terrible. They have to accomodate for a huge population and vast cultures so I think that they do o.k. They have 3 restaurants that you can make reservations at- Mexican, Japanese and Caribe. There is also a restaurant on the beach side. They don't have a welcome packet if you go like we did through Expedia, but if you travel with a group- Apple, Sunquest, etc. they have an orientation. We took the plunge and had our photo's done by Jose' in the photo shop near the big pool. He was wonderful. He takes you and family out and takes digital photo's all over the complex including the beach-you can have as many dress changes as you want, couples or singles, it is totally up to you. My husband and I were amazed at how wonderful they turned out. He will put as many as you want on a CD for $5 a photo or even print some out for $8. each. We selected 25 pictures on the CD. This is well worth looking into. Just note that at this time he did not take credit cards. Overall the resort is o.k. There is not a lot to do unless you go off the resort except sunbath (which is what we wanted to do), or water sports off the beach. Give it a try for a week and see what you think. The beach has changed since the last time we were in Dominican. They had a storm and now there is more seaweed than before. They do what they can to clean up. It's the Dominican- you go there for the weather and relaxation-if you want total luxury than stay in the US or pay a huge amount of money to stay at a palace resort. We ended up paying around $800.per person, per week- all inclusive-airfare, hotel, food, drinks. We will go back to Dominican and try yet another resort to see how they all compare. Satisfied with 2 weeks of Sun and relaxation!!!  
<Date>Apr 9, 2006
