<Author>David Lee
<Content>Much better than expected - a lovely resort We鈥檝e just got back from 2 weeks at IFA Villas Bavaro. We booked this, then got a bit worried by the mixed reviews! We鈥檙e quite experienced travellers staying in both top-end and also more budget places of all types. Overall rate the IFA resort very highly and as one of the most relaxing holidays for a long time, in excellent surroundings.First impressions of our room (1045), one of the many single-storey villas on the inland side of the complex, weren鈥檛 too positive. It was spacious but quite dark and furniture/bathroom basic and dated, and would no doubt disappoint some people. However it had all essentials and everything was clean, comfortable and the daily maid service was friendly and we quickly settled in. All rooms have nice small terraces, free cable TV showing local and some US channels, and a safe to store valuables (daily charge 2 USD). While the 鈥榁illas鈥?part of the resort was mostly peaceful those rooms nearest the stage area got a bit of noise from about 8pm to midnight, although we were fine with it. We were impressed by the immaculate grounds and overall peaceful feel of the place. The walk from the Villas area to the beach took about 15 minutes through lovely well-maintained gardens and seemed wheelchair friendly throughout. Along the way you pass various bars, restaurants, shops, activity areas There鈥檚 a free hotel 鈥渂us鈥?to the beach, but seemed unnecessary for most -it takes a small road round the edge of the complex 鈥?the main area of the resort mostly car free. The beach itself is excellent, fine white sand and palm trees. The 鈥淚FA section鈥?is spacious, clean and easy to find quiet areas well away from the organised activities. There are only a few areas with good shade so have to be lucky - or early - to get these but you can also move sun-beds under the shade of the many palm trees. The warm clean sea is sheltered by a reef about 500 meters out and there鈥檚 free use of kayaks, small sailing dinghies (an hour at a time, needs security deposit between 30-100USD depending on what you use). You can pay to hire bigger sailboats or for other activities (diving/parasailing etc). There are quite a lot of speed-boats, powered hangliders etc but it didn鈥檛 spoil the very relaxing feel of the beach for us.The two main buffet restaurants have a nice atmosphere and always had a wide range of things on offer (including some local dishes), with quality from average to quite good, and though nothing spectacular, we enjoyed the experience - a good range of fresh fruit was always on offer. We tried three of the speciality restaurants 鈥?鈥渋nteresting鈥?interpretations of Mexican and Japanese food but still fun. We were alcohol-free so cant comment on the booze 鈥?there was no real juice on offer, mostly sugary squash, but this was offset by the endless, mostly excellent fresh fruit. The beach restaurant bar does a good lunchtime meal with quite good choice in a good setting and chance for a make your own burger/hot dog binge alongside healthier options. The staff were mostly friendly and attentive. Other guests (seemed mostly an equal mix of US, Canadian, British, German, French Spanish) seemed good-natured and we didn鈥檛 see any rowdiness.鈥?what we saw of the evening entertainment seemed OK if a bit samey, merengue dancing, competitions etc Overall we thought it was great and really liked the relaxed feel of an all inclusive - minimal decision making in a very attractive setting. We did travel out independently to Santo Domingo - and beyond - as well as doing one of the 鈥減ackaged鈥?excursions and this added a lot to the experience. Weather was excellent.

<Content>A good place for the budget Stayed at this resort end of February '06. We usually stay at time-shares so all-inclusive resort was a change. These are very insulated environments. It is important to remember we are guests in another country. The manegement was professional and efficiently dealt with inappropriate behaviors. Guests were expected to wear shirts  shoes in the dining areas although the beach bar was more relaxed. Specialty restaurants had to be reserved a day ahead. Standing in the line to get a seating was a great way to meet other people. We enjoyed the food at all the dining areas. Children were accepted but did not run wild. We found all the staff friendly and tried to make your visit enjoyable. The dive-shop (Neptuno) was very good. They offer a resort course and dives for different skills. They were very thorough and we would recommend them for any divers. The evening entertaiment area was very close to some guest rooms. Some might avoid this accomodation.The beach was a short, pleasant walk from the main areas.Above average for the price.

<Author>GlobetrotterSue
<Content>The spirit of the Dominican This resort is typical Dominican style i.e no frills, no hurry.If you want luxury up your budget and look at some of the other superb hotels in Bavaro.We were on a tight post Christmas budget but in urgent need of sunshine and 2 weeks at the IFA didn't break the bank. I was a bit nervous having read the mixed reviews but bit the bullet and will share my findings with you....THE ACCOMODATIONWe stayed in the villas(rm 1025) and it was ok but quite hard work for 2 weeks. The pillows were well ready for the skip and I was convinced that I had a water bed the mattress was so wobbly! The lighting is not good for us girls and I dare say it must have looked like Coco the clown had arrived with the dodgy makeup! Towels were generally ok. Maids did a good job. Rooms in need of a bit of cheering up but were tolerable.THE FOODNot brilliant but always able to cobble something together at the buffet all be it a chip buttie! A lot of traditional foods served at all times. There are not enough staff in the buffets and often there was a bit of a wait for a table or a cup of coffee (only available with breakfast). The al a carte restaraunts required booking a day ahead. Bookings were supposed to be from 4pm but the line was huge by 3pm and all the best slots taken by those lucky enough to be near the front. This system needs reviewing. I can recommend the Mexican but didn't bother with the japanese or caribe.THE DRINKSThere are 4 bars and a beach bar. Most drinks served via worlitzer and were very flat and sugery. There is a good cocktail list and I think we tried most drinks with varying degrees of success! None of the bars have enough seating and folk ended up sprawled on sunbeds sipping their marguaritas - not so far to fall I guess as I disagree with previous reviews saying the drinks are watered down!That said if you get tipsy you are lucky as the service can be very slow depending upon the bar staff on duty. On the whole pleasant and friendly with limited English though the girls in particular try very hard to communicate.You are issued with 2 water bottles on arrival and these can be filled up from tanks at the bars. A dollar to the maid ensures extra bottles are placed in your fridge every few days.THE GUESTS AND POOLSPredominantly French/Canadian/American/German. Many of whom may not have grasped the principle of a relaxing holiday and were up and silly o'clock putting towels on sunbeds. very tempting to collect them up at 6am and put them in a pile especially since many of their owners did not appear until well into the afternoon by which time the more leisurely travellers were covered in grass stains and sweat as the few beds with parasols were taken. This behaviour needs addressing at not only this but all resorts where it is allowed to happen. The pools themselves - 1. Known as the quiet pool as there is no animation. However, come lunchtime the nighttime entertainment crew are out practicing their routines and its like Sunday Night at The Palladium!. A bit annoying at times. The music at the pool is, I'm sure, some form of torture as the same half dozen tracks are played over and over. Take your ipod! 2. The Big pool fun and games most of the day with the animation team. Lots of kids and lilos - got the picture..?3. The Little pool Tiny - about 20 sunbeds booked by the time the sun comes up. very close to the restaraunt so don't pick this one unless you are happy for people to gawp at you over their omelette!THE BEACHLovely but smallish and very popular.Get down there very early if you want a sunbed. There is a bar and a restaraunt so you need not go up to the main resort if you are cosy i.e managed to bag a sunbed!There is a fair sized shopping area but get your bargaining head on and know how much you are prepared to pay. The guys are very persistant.WHAT ELSEThe Jellyfish Restaraunt is on the beach right next door to the IFA and is fab. Friendy and welcoming place serving great value seafood.Excellent service, cool trance muscic, wonderful deck area to look out to sea. Give it a visit or you will be missing out on a treat away from the buffet and sugery drinks!WOULD I STAY AT THE IFA AGAIN?With a restricted budget yes but would try to save a bit harder or sting a rich relative for the extra money to stay at a slightly more up market hotel.If you like Butlins, you will like the IFA.Accept it for what it is and have a great time.

<Content>A-Z EVERYTHING U NEED 2 NO My husband and I just returned from the Lopesan Villas. We stayed from the 12-16th of February. Honestly, we breathed a sigh of relief once we arrived. It wasn't as bad as we thought it may be. It was actually very nice. After reading the reviews we called ahead of time and requested a room by the ocean, they were so nice, they did it for us! However,below I will list everything you need to know by category-ufortuantly we will not return to this hotel! Pay the extra money and GO ENJOY yourself!Staff: Pleasant, accomodating. They do not speak English! Rooms: Well, O.K. they are not the best. If you get stuck with two double beds, go up immediatly and put your name on the list for the next available king bed. These rooms are much bigger and nicer! The rooms are the worst parts of the hotel. They are very clean, although they are also very old. They were do-able for a short vacation.Resturants: Well, when you check in they will give you a map of Hotel along with resturants. This leaves out VERY important stuff. It only lists three restaurants, two buffets and bech bar. First, DO NOT GO TO BEACH BAR. It was AWEFUL. Second, both buffets are O.K., but the food was only average at best. What they leave out are the three other resturants, Japonaise, Caribe and Mexican. These are much better than the buffets but you need to make reservations the day before! They say at 4-7, they actually start at 3, so get there early! Also, this part of the hotel is the nicest! The entertainment, two great bars and nice resturants make up this end of Hotel! Hang out over here in the evening! BARS: Well, we had warm beer and aweful drinks the entire trip! The frozen drinks were aweful! Rum comes out of a sprayer, and it must be watered down! The alcohol is AWEFUL! The drinks were AWEFUL! The best bar is the Captains Bar, very elegant looking, better srinks than anywhere else. Also, the only place to find cappacinos!Entertainment: Not so good.Pools: Very nice! However, keep in mind there really is no swim up bar in the one pool, and none in the rest of them. No one serves you drinks either. Beach: Beautiful!!!!!!!!!! Lots of topless people though!Shopping: If you walk to the right of the beach you see alot of shops, good deals!Now, FYI, I have been sick for two days. I went to Dr., and they say food poison. Sometimes, in resorts where they have buffets all the time, things just are not clean or are left out to long..This is the case at the Lopesan Villas. BE CAREFUL bring meds with you! Also, bring bug spray, at the resort it was $10.00! I got eaten up pretty bad!!! Also, bring a sweater at night it was a little chilly!Overall, spend the extra money and stay somewhere else!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wouldn't Return We just returned from a two week stay at Ifa Villas Bavaros from Jan 26 to Feb 9th.We were at room 1211, 1210 and 1207. There were 7 of us and I know we won't go back. We flew sky service, which was fine. Tiny seats and no room but I guess that's normal. Check in went fine but once we told the lobby assistants our room number they acted like we were asking them to donate blood! Then we learned our rooms were like a 10 minute walk from the lobby which was still about 8 minutes from the beach. Thankfully they had a trolly, sort of like a golf cart with a trailor. They drive a little crazy but it saved us a lot of time. (It was however really noisy and would wake us up early in the morning and late at night when it would drive by). The rooms looked like something from a 1970's cheap motel. I was disappointed to open the frige and find two bottles of water and that's all. We were expecting a stocked mini fridge with pop, beer, etc...nope. We were then informed we had to keep our two bottles of water and refill them oursleves at the bars. When we lost them, after using them for 10 days, it was a real hassle to get them replaced. The service really wasn't very good at all. We often waited for 15 or more minutes for a drink at the buffets and the bars. Some staff were often rude! The food was, well, mostly okay. If you could get a reservation for one of the restaurants you were sitting pretty. The food was awesome and the service was exceptional but if you were stuck with the buffets, have fun!! I was really disappointed with the lack of fresh fruit juice. All the juice was really sugary and powder based. The beach was beautiful!!! The disco was fun, but always consistant. Also difficult to get a drink there. The swim up bar was a joke. You could sit there but unless you stood up on a stool and got their attention ( which is way harder than it sounds) you would get NO service. We went on the Saona Island day trip. DO THAT IT WAS AMAZING! We also went on the Caribbean Festival boat trip which was also fun. I wish I had more good to say. This resort calls itself a 4 star. Please don't be fooled!

<Content>Worst all-inclusive in Punta Cana I have never written a hotel review before but I feel I must this time. We are 2 middle aged couples who have been in Punta Cana 10 times in 9 different all-inclusive resorts. We went to IFA Villas Bavaro November 2005. I must say this is by far the worst hotel we have ever been there.The day we arrived the other couple had to get their room 3704 changed in the middle of the night because their air conditioning didn鈥檛 work. Because of the rush they left a full bottle of shampoo in the washroom. Next day they asked for it but it never appeared and nothing was done about it. We were assigned room 3703 on the ground floor. On the third day I woke up walking on the sewage of the rooms above because the sewer was blocked. They had to change us to a room on a second floor. Some other details about the rooms and accesses: Public walkways had the lights removed (I guess to save electricity), actually ripped right off the wall. You could see on the walls where they had been. Same thing in the balconies. Twice they put towels ripped in half in the bathroom; one half for each person. The pillows were very old and full of matted balls.In regards to the rest: Clean beach towels were never available.70% of the reclining chairs on the beach were broken.The gym was a joke.Non motorized sports were not free. They charged us US$15 for the use of a hobbie-cat for an hour. There are no pedal boats.The food was the worst we have ever had in the Dominican Republic: Juices are fake, marmalade and jam of the cheapest kind available in the country, same for all alcoholic beverages. Oil was un-edible, one day at breakfast the milk was sour.At the Caribean a-la-carte restaurant there was no regular wine available. If you wanted to drink wine with your dinner, you had to pay extra. The service at that restaurant was so lousy we stood up and left after 10 minutes.Buffet food was poor to say the least.All in all a hotel without love, without care for the customers. Please take notice that all 4 of us are South Americans, therefore it is not a matter of cultural differences. Also what I said at the beginning; we are comparing this so called 3 1/2 or 4 star hotel with 8 other all-inclusive hotels in the same area and with the same number of stars.Our advice is, no matter how cheap they offer this hotel to you, pick something else.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>IFA Bavaro My friend and i stayed at this hotel from Feb 1st to Feb 5th. The walk to the beach is five minutes. There are 3 restaurants on site and four bars. I would recommend this hotel to: couples, families and senior citizens. This hotel offers a lot of pool activities and water sports. If you are however traveling on your own (not from an agency nor with a big group) make sure you keep busy b.c. it may get a little slow at times. My friend and I booked a day trip to Saona island, we left at 7am and got back at 7pm. If you like sailing this is a trip for you.We also went on a 2 hour snorkeling adventure, which included a speed boat racing-oh yeaaa- very fun. You have to pay for these out of your own pocket, we paid $120 ea for both but def. worth it :)You can buy these trips from representatives that hang out at the lobby/reception at the hotel. Look for Caramel, he was very nice to us and informative.Remember to bring: cash, there is an atm machine on site but it does not take for example american express, and it was out of service when we needed it the most. A waterproof camera, they sell them at the shop at the hotel but it will cost you $44!!! A dictionary maybe useful. We would def. return to Punta Cana.

<Author>Wife_in_Texas
<Content>Have an Open Mind!!! We got back late last night from a 4-day visit to this hotel. Here are our thoughts:I hate to admit it (don't want to sound like a spoiled-rotten tourist), but my first impression of the hotel was not the best. The grounds were good, but the room was very basic, even a little run-down. But the negatives stop right here.Honestly, we had a great time. If you're looking for something luxurious, this is not your stop. The whole focus here was the laid-back atmosphere. The entertainers were awesome; they did everything to make you feel right at home. They really were the best part of our stay.The beach was absolutely gorgeous, clean, and perfect.The food was good, and they tried to accommodate all sorts of nationalities (from French toast to mashed potatoes and salad for breakfast).There were very few people from the US, so if you've never been out of the country, you're in for a surprise. To us it was quite interesting getting a glimpse of all the different cultures, but you definitely need to have an open mind.All in all, we loved it, and would definitely go back and stay there again, now that we have our priorities in check and know what to expect.If you do decide to go, make sure to have a private session with the photographer at the beach. My husband and I did and we're still drooling over the pictures in the Caribbean sun.

<Content>great value and a fantastic beach We have just returned from a week long vacation at ifa villas bavaro and had a wonderfull time. Our supplier was Nolitours. The representative at the resort was very helpful in guiding us through the available tours that were being offered. We were in the ocean area of the resort. The other two areas of the resort are the village and the villas. Stay away from the villas if possible. It is a fifeteen minute walk to the beach. Nolitours and Airtransat vacations have a contract that guarantees that you will be located at the ocean or the village. Everything about this resort is excellent especially the beach which is breathtaking. The only thing that We found that was subpar was the quality of the evening entertainment. The entertainers work very hard but the shows seem inferior to some other resorts we have stayed at. Some of the negative reviews I have read about this reort must have come from some very pessimistic people because there is very little fact to their stories. My wife and I agree that this is a resort that we will visit again. We reccommend it highly for anyone looking for a great vacation.

<Author>Honey510
<Content>Good value for money My boyfriend and I stayed at this resort 14th - 28th November 2005. On arrival we were rather disappointed as we were led to believe that this was 4 star accommodation as opposed to 3 star, but we couldn't really complain considering the price we paid, it was definitely good value.We stayed in the 3000 block near the pool. The room was basic but large and clean. We were initially a bit disappointed that our room was at the back, overlooking the gardens, but we later realised this wasn't such a bad thing because the rooms facing the pool must have been very noisy when the entertainment started.When we arrived we didn't hear another English voice for 2 days. The place was overrun with Germans! We did eventually meet other English/American/Canadian people but they were few and far between.The food in the buffet restaurants was ok as long as you got there early. We found some of the food to be lukewarm if we went for dinner after 9pm. Definitely book for the El Caribe restaurant as the food was delicious. Don't bother with the Japanese though. You can book for the following night between 9-11am at the desk behind the Lobby Bar.The entertainment was a bit lame - not our cup of tea. Some of the stuff made you cringe - it was like being at Butlins. Stay in the bars instead!!!El Capitan is a nice bar, as is the one over the far pool. Visited the nightclub on a couple of occasions and lets just say you need to have had a fair few beers before you go. If they are not playing cheesy 80's rubbish (e.g. I Will Survive) you have to contend with nothing but salsa music. It's ok in moderation but after an hour it starts to grate. We had a laugh though.The beach was gorgeous and we never had a problem findings sunbeds there, or round the pool.We went on a trip to La Palimera and Saona Island which was a great day out. We travelled there on catamaran and back on a speed boat. We also stopped for some fantastic snorkelling.Also went on the Outback Safari which was average. The guide was very knowledgeable and lunch was nice but we got thrown about so much on the truck, I banged my head twice. We went boogie boarding in the morning but the sea was so rough I spent more time sprawled in the sand with the board on top of me!! All in all the holiday was good value for money as we got a cancellation but I wouldn't pay full price to stay there.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Its cheap, but not worth the savings My boyfriend and I went to IFA for a week in mid-October. We are 28 and 30yrs old and both have travelled extensively and have lived abroad. I personally lived in India for 14mths and travelled through South East Asia, so I knew what to expect going to a poorer country. We normally do not do all-inclusive, resort-type vacations but have had a little experience with them. I've been to Cuba and Mexico as well so I was hoping my DR experience would match those wonderful trips. Unfortunatley, that was not the case this time. I would not recommend going to Punta Cana. Perhaps Puerto Plata would've been better for us, but we'll never know. Here are our thoughts from our trip - we hope it helps:RoomsRooms were adequate for a 3 star hotel. We stayed in the 3000 block of rooms, which is midway between the beach and the front lobby. We had water pressure issues 2 out of 7 days we were there (the water was turned off for hours at a time for 鈥渕aintenance鈥?. Air vents in all rooms are connected so you can smell the smoke from other people鈥檚 rooms, which was an annoyance for us non-smokers. There are no non-smoking rooms or blocks. The paint etc needs updating but not a big deal. Don鈥檛 expect beauty in the rooms.ServiceThe service was okay with some exceptions. If you tip you will get more attention and care but overall the service was alright. The staff definitely work hard. Tips are greatly appreciated.BeachThe beach was nice, white sand with warm, aquamarine blue water. Visibility in the ocean is poor for snorkeling etc. The beach chairs get uncomfortable after a while; the plastic hurts your back. There are a few chairs that are cushioned but unless you鈥檙e an early riser, they will most likely be taken before you get to the beach. There are no umbrellas for use so you have to find a spot under a palm tree. The animation team has sessions on the beach in the morning and afternoons and can be quite loud. They will try to recruit you to participate and can be annoying if you鈥檙e looking to just relax, read a book and listen to the ocean waves. They also play the same music every day.FoodBreakfast sucks. The quality of food is poor and it鈥檚 always the same. Lunch is good if you eat at the main restaurant by the reception. Don鈥檛 eat at the beach restaurant, its terrible.Dinner was hit and miss. At the main restaurant the food was generally good with variety each night. The Mexican restaurant has good and bad dishes, however make sure you鈥檙e comfortable with your partner cause you鈥檒l be sharing some very intimate (aka smelly!) moments with them afterwards. We were told to avoid the Japanese restaurant by some other people we talked to at the resort so we never tried it. The beach restaurant FOR DINNER was good. We went two nights in a row and other people we talked to about it were happy with it as well. It鈥檚 also lovely to sit by the ocean and feel the cool breeze while you eat (which also helps keep the mosquitoes away).Snacks were pretty much non-existent. We were told we could only get snacks during the day at the beach restaurant, but the 鈥榮nacks鈥?were actually the horrible lunch they offered there.One of us has a very sensitive stomach and other one doesn鈥檛. Both of us got diarrhea despite taking pepto bismol pills everyday and acidophilus pills before we went. We did not overeat and we did not drink alcohol so we were pretty cautious about our eating habits and drinking habits but were effected by the food regardless.AnimationThe animation team works very hard and after watching them you feel sympathy for what they鈥檙e doing. They basically work their ass off to get people to participate in their activities throughout the day but the problem is the activities aren鈥檛 our cup of tea. For some people, maybe with young children or people looking to be more outgoing, they might have enjoyed the animation team. But for us it was mostly embarrassing, cheesy, low-brow or annoying. However, we respect the animation team鈥檚 purpose, however we wish it was designated to one area of the resort. We felt we could not escape them because there was something going on wherever we went. There are three swimming pools and the beach and the animation staff were doing something at almost all of them. There was one pool where the animation team did not work at but it was the smallest pool and it had only three umbrellas, which were usually occupied.ToursWe went on one tour with a tour company called the Bavaro Runners, where we went to visit a sugar cane plantation, a family-owned coffee, cocoa and fruit farm, lunch and horseback riding on the beach. Overall, it was a great tour and a wonderful way to see some of the island culture. Our guide was personable and knowledgeable. However, if you are prone to motion sickness at all you should avoid doing any tours that involve a lot of driving. The main road from the airport to the resort is fine, but when we did the tour, we went off the main road a lot and it made one of us extremely ill. There are humungous pot holes everywhere. You can鈥檛 avoid them. There are better roads in India!When you book a tour, do it through your tour agency instead of buying it off of one of the independent guys working in the reception area because your tour agency will be insured in case you get into an accident. The tour agency will be happy to switch dates if you happen to be sick on the day of your scheduled tour and will have guides that speak English or whatever language you speak. We saw other groups doing the same tour as us but with guides speaking in their native language (French or Spanish).MiscExpect mosquitoes, especially if you鈥檙e going during the wet season, which we did. They can get into your room and bother you at night, if you鈥檙e finicky about these things. Wear repellant and they鈥檒l most likely leave you alone.Prices at the hotel stores are ridiculously over priced. Beware! At one store, they wanted to charge us $10USD for a small bag of chips and a chocolate bar. Also we were witness to a situation where another resort guest was purchasing a drink at one of the bars and the barman blatantly over charged him. We called him on it and then he returned some of the money, but he was not apologetic and it was still overpriced. We think that this must happen a lot since guests don鈥檛 know what the prices should be and are gullible. We think that the hotel should have price lists of the special drinks that have to be paid for.The sun is very intense so wear protective sun block even if it is overcast or cloudy.Beware of the guys in white shirts that say 鈥淩oyal鈥?on it because they will try to befriend you, then waste your time trying to sell you on a timeshare. The guys work on the resort so you will see them everywhere and they actually work for the resort. They鈥檙e aggressive and annoying. The resort also sets up a market by the main pool and the sellers are very aggressive. It was annoying because you feel like you鈥檙e just a walking dollar sign and can鈥檛 let your guard down to relax.Also the security guards can be creepy. They hit on one of us (the girl) blatantly. He was staring hard at me and then whispered that he thought I was 鈥渂eautiful鈥? while he was touching his genitals. Ick.Bring US dollars or use the ATM machine, which dispenses DR pesos. Canadian dollars are accepted reluctantly or not at all. You can however, exchange your cash at the hotel lobby but don't expect a great rate.I wish we could recommend this place, but unfortunately it was too disappointing.

<Author>bonbini1
<Content>Nice place- and a good bargain! We returned yesterday from this resort and we both had a wonderful vacation. We're a couple in our mid forties, and this was my 10th visit to an all inclusive resort in the DR. This is a very nice property for the money. I have to disagree with the previous review. We found the staff to be very friendly and helpful at all times and they always returned a smile, regardless of if we were tipping or not. The food was good- and we never saw anything spoiled. As for the previous comments about the birds- unless you have a bird phobia- I can't imagine this being a problem. Anywhere you have an open air restaurant- a bird or two will be flying in occasionally for a snack. Upon check-in I requested a room close to the beach and we were placed in the Ocean Village section on the beach and even had an ocean view- which pleased us both. The room was clean and our beds were fine. There were only a few differences between this resort and some of the higher priced ones where we've stayed previously- for example- only water in the mini-fridge (no cokes and beers)- not a problem for us. No room service- again not a problem for us, as we never use it at resorts that have it. No waiters taking drink orders on the beach and bringing them to you- again no problem for us as the bar isn't too far to walk to. No coffee maker in the room- which would have been nice, but wasn't a problem. We loved that the resort never seemed too crowded and that we didn't have to get up at the crack of dawn to get a shady spot on that gorgeous beach. There were spots available at all times of day- at the beach or by the pools. We swam in 2 of the 3 pools and they were very pleasant. We dined at the Japanese and the Mexican restaurants and both enjoyed them, even though it's not the typical Japanese and Mexican food that we are used to! As for the vendors and time share people- they are only trying to make a living. All we did is say no, gracias in a polite and friendly manner- and we were never hasseled. Yes, when shopping the vendors will ask outlandishly high prices for the merchandise- but they always will come down to a fair price. Of course they want to make as much money as possible- but they don't ever expect someone to pay the initial asking price- kind of like a yard sale! Even though we only saw a few other guests from the US- we never felt uncomfortable or unable to communicate with the staff or the guests from other countries. Learning a little Spanish and German can be really helpful when visiting the DR! We only did one excursion this time and it was riding the quads-and it was a fun afternoon. We truly enjoyed our visit to Villas Bavaro and I wouldn't hesitate to recommend this property. I will definitely be returning to the DR again soon!!  
<Date>Nov 1, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Family of 10 - Laughter/Fun/Good Time Let me just state that we just returned from PUNTA CANA and the entire family ages 16-55 enjoyed the trip. Punta Cana was worth the money and value for a group of different personalities.Below are my suggestions if your're planning on staying at the IFA Villas Bavaro and what to do if your going to Punta Cana, DR.AIRPORT- Before you get off the plane, check yourself in the mirror and say HOLA they snap your picture for you to remember, (like going to an amusement park) you can purchase on your return. Driving to the resort the island is not a plush, green island but pulling up to the resort was nice.HOTEL- You check-in get a wrist band, and your set for food, beverages and shuttle services. The rooms were average,  don't forget your wash cloths they don't have those....only handtowels. The a-c worked great. This is not a 4 star resort, don't go looking for that. The hotel grounds reminded me of camp-like setting, but it's exactly as it looks in the brochures. The food wasn't great, but when your're hungry you'll eat what's given. I stuck to breads and pasta. The teenagers to french fries  chicken.ACTIVITIES- The Bavaro beach sand was wonderful, not the kind were you walk on and your feet are like hot potatoes...it's fine warm sand. The hotel offers water aerobics, line dancing, night movies at the bar  music around the main pool and beach. At 9 they have a show, at 11pm the beach party. However, it wasn't much to do between 6-11pm-- You have to wait for the party to get started. I also recommend booking your excursions before you get to Punta Cana. We had sooo much fun on the Outback Safari Tour, we learned soo much about the Dominican island from this day trip . I also sugggest the Party Boat- (Con Tiki??)... However, don't snorkel and drink rum punch, some of the group members got sick later on in the trip.. :)*(Funny, they were the only ones who snorkeled  dranked rum punch. UMMM!All in all, we had a great time, we all laughed so hard we will all remember something from that trip...it was great time of laughter, fun and a good vacation gettaway. I'm even thinking of learning Spanish so the next time if we return I can carry a conversation or two.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fun, fun, fun.... We recently returned from IFA Bavaro Villas June 17, 2005 and had a wonderful time. We have traveled throughout various Caribbean Islands and to be honest after reading the reviews and the 3.5 star rating I was a little nervous. Much to my surprise it was much nicer, cleaner and the staff friendlier than at the 4 or 5 star resorts we have visited. CHECK-IN: Upon check-in you do have staff present who does speak the English language and will make every effort possible to accommodate your needs. Let me back up, there were 2 families traveling together for a total of 4 adults and 4 children. When we arrived we were put in two different villas. The villas are anywhere from 1100 - 4500. We were put in 4200 and 3100. We asked the staff if there was a possibility to stay closer and they put us next door to one another.FOOD: We never went hungry. When traveling with teenage children they tend to be very picky about what they eat. At the IFA that was not a problem. They offer a variety of food so that everyone can find what they are looking to eat that particular day. Please try the Dominica Restaurant located within the resort. You must make reservations 24 hours in advance. It is definately worth it. The Dominica is a restaurant that offers food selections that the people of Dominican Republic eat at their homes. Wonderful server in the Dominican Restaurant named Mildred. She makes those who visit the Dominican Restaurant feel like they are queen of the Dominican Republic. We loved the treatment we received so we ate there every other day. Hee Hee!! Mexican restaurant is also very good choice, however, mosquitos were present there. I guess those pesty bugs liked the Mexican aroma as well. My husband loved the Mexican restaurant. Once again, 24 hour notice. DRINKS: Bartenders can make anything your little heart desires. Most drinks when traveling with minor children are without liquor unless you as the adult request it. Must try the MAMA WANNA. Its a liquor for the MAN. I thought it much to strong for me, but you need to give it a little try. Your on vacation, why not!!!ACTIVITIES: Plenty of them. On the beach, at the pool located closest to the lobby and in the evening at the theatrical stage which is located behind the lobby and nearest the largest swimming pool. Yes there are 3 pools, 2 pretty large pools and one smaller one that is located in the 4000 block of rooms. The animation team there is superior to all other Caribbean resorts we have visited. You have to experience the fun with HAPPY BOY (that is his name on his name tag). He will have you laughing the night away!!SOUVENIERS: When you go to the beach, shops on both sides. BARGAIN!!! If they say $68, you say 5 and go from there. They will eventually give you a calculator and say give me a price. Be prepared to walk away in order to get your price. Enjoy the resort, the staff and your vacation. It's very fun at the IFA.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>It was a real vacation Me and my fiance just came back to New York after a 10 day stay at the IFA Villas Bavaro Resort. Overall it was a great experience, we are now relaxed, tanned and gained weight(unfortunately!)... Rooms: Very clean, very basic, TV is mostly Spanish, also some American channels like CNN, Fox 5 available. Nice balkony viewing the pool and palm trees. Only few minutes walking from the beach. Room service punctual, clean bath towels everyday,garbage taken out, beds made, room cleaned;thanks to Juanita, our cleaning lady.We left her a 10 dollar tip. Pools and bars: 3 pools,very clean,the one next to the main lobby has a tiki bar, other pools also have nearby bars open from early morning. Only local drinks available. The only beer is Dominican  Presidente beer which is pretty light. Do not forget to try exotic drinks like Banana mama (you can ask them to add Rum as well) and Coco Loco Food: PLENTY of food.....Be careful, one tends to overeat...I did not get sick at all, but my fiancee had some diarrhea mainly from eating and drinking a lot. Coffee is excellent( I think even better than Starbucks) It is Dominican Coffee, the best brand is Santa Domingo, I bought plenty of it on my way back. Restaurante Colibri offers good breakfast, you can customize your omlette by mixing cheese, mushrooms, sausage, tomatoes and ask the cook to make you an omelette. For lunch we preferred the beach restaurant to get some light and fast food mostly grilled chicken/fish/meatball or salad/fruits. For dinner I recommend making a reservation for Mexican restaurant. The tacos (chicken or beef) are especially good. Anything you eat at the stationary section is good. Do not even bother to make a reservation at the Dominican restaurant, nothing special is served except this drink called  mama juana which is believed to be a local sexual enhancer.Otherwise Restaurante Colibri is good for dinner too, I recommend fish or chicken rather than beef, for some reason beef was hard and tasteless.As for fish, poisson is the best. Lots of deserts every day,make sure you try the rice puding. Beach: Flawless. Beautiful soft white sand,pine trees, still and light blue water not so cold, cool enough to refresh your tanning body. We spent most of our days at the beach or at the pools. Animators have daily beach programmes, I took a few merenge and salsa lessons (they don't let you leave the hotel if you can't learn how to dance!!), some aerobic lessons as well. We also rented a canoe and went for snorkeling ( included in the all inclusive package).  Shopping: Hotel has lots of little shops for great gifts like cigars, jewellery ( DR or is well known for Larimar which is a blue gemstone found only in this island and very fine amber), paintings. Right next to the hotel at the beach on the right side is a bazaar where you can buy all this stuff and more. Make sure to bargain!! Offer 1/5 of the price they tell you, you'll get it. Now here is a little tip; if you walk on the beach to the left for about 15 minutes you will find an  Art Galery where tens of paintings are literally hanging on the strings in rows like a festival. The colors are amazing. The pictures are real oil paintings, the styles are very local, themes are mostly native women, fruits or symbols of ancient Indian Gods. You get the best prices there. The sellers are very nice,speak English well, especially Rafael. Still make sure you bargain. We bought 5 paintings and lots of other local goods.We did not have money on us, they drove us back to our hotel and accepted credit card. Staff: Very friendly,warm. Service is fast. Try to learn a few Spanish words, they do appreciate the effort. Other: We took a daily trip to Santa Domingo. We saw the first cathedral built in America and the house of Colombus's son. It is a poor city but I think it is worth to get out the resort at least for a day and get to know the country you visit. The trip is arranged by many travel agents, can be booked at the main lobby, we paid 72 USD per person.There is also a complimentary shuttle from the main lobby to a casino nearby. It is small but still we had a lot of fun especially playing blackjack. In the shuttle they give 20 dolar worth of free coupons per person.  Health: Medications are over the counter in DR and the hotel has a pharmacy and a doctor if needed. Still I brought some medications for pain, itching, diarhea and nausea from US. Make sure you bring mosquito repellents with you as there are many mosquitos around. We also took prophylactic medication for malaria. If you will not leave the hotel resort then malaria prophylaxis is not recommended as there have been very few cases from the resorts, but malaria is endemic in DR so if you are planning to go out of the resort and go around then you need to take malaria prophylaxis, so you need to see your doctor about 4 weeks prior to your trip to get your prescription. Before I went to this hotel, I was tired, stressed and overworked, needed a real vacation. I got what I needed, I stepped into a world of clean, beautiful beach, pools, unlimited food and drinks, lovely people. I did not even carry a purse or ID with me. Just the wrist band given from the hotel reception to all the guests.....I highly recommend this hotel. We probably will not be able to go back again because we are planning to explore other countries for our next vacations.  
<Date>May 31, 2005

<Content>Good Value for the money We visited for one week Feb.5th- Feb12th 2005 The rooms were not bad but could use some modernization the beds were hard and not very comfortable the pillows were flat the comforters were old looking.The bathroom and the dresser in our room had ants but we brought our own bug spray and that took care of them. <Content>Fell in love with D.R. way of life!!! My friend and I travelled to the Dominican Republic Nov 20, 2003. Our flight there was excellent, the transportation provided to the resort was great as well. Our check in was prompt and the service was excellent. Both my friend and I only speak English and had no difficulty communicating with the staff. We spent most of our time at the Bar Margarita and had the best food and friendly service at the Las Careyna's? buffet (closest to the Margarita Bar). Our room was kept clean and towel art was a regular occurence on our beds. We had no problems with air conditioning but did find that hot water could be hard to come by just before traditional mealtimes(8am/5-6pm)but otherwise our stay was excellent!! The resort grounds were immaculate as was the beach, not an ounce of seaweed or garbage to be found. I will definately go back and stay at this resort as well as recommend it to others!! I made some great friends while on this trip, including some locals that I have kept in touch with. I am looking forward to going back early 2005. We also took a couple of day trips outside the resort as well as attending a club that allows locals, what a blast! Email me for photos or suggestions.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Paradise for the right Price We visited this resort June 20-27, 2004 for our honeymoon. Our flights were on time, no delays, and check-in was a breeze. From the moment we arrived, we noticed the kindness and friendly atmosphere from the people who worked there. Our room was in the little villas which was very private and very clean. Contrary to a few other reviews I've read, there were absolutely no insects of any kind in our room. Nor were there any in the rooms of the many people we met there. I took the advice of travelers who went before me ... I left a small gift for our maid - Esther - every day. She was so very sweet. Every day she left fresh flowers in a glass of water on the bathroom sink. One day she made a little trail of flowers along the edge of the bathtub and on the sink counter. Another day, she made swans out of the bathtowels and put them in the middle of the bed. This reflected the positive attitude and helpfulness of every employee we met on this resort. The first day we were there, we came back to our room to find a gift of fresh fruit and a bottle of rum with a letter from the management congratulating us on our marriage. How thoughtful was that? :)You've all heard many stories about the food. For breakfast, I had a freshly made omelet everyday with a variety of meats, vegetables, and cheeses to choose from. Every meal offered a huge variety of breads, rolls, crescents, and biscuits. There is a cold food bar with different salads. There is a fresh fruit bar. The hot food bar always had a beef dish, fish of some kind, chicken and/or ham. There is a pasta bar with different kinds of sauces and a chef to cook it for you. Was the food gourmet quality? No. Did you pay for gourmet quality? No. But the food is good and plentiful. And we never got sick the entire time we were there. We kept bottled water in our refrigerator in our room and used that to brush our teeth, just in case.The beach is beautiful. It takes no more than 10 or 15 minutes to walk through the resort to the beach. There is also a shuttle that will take you back and forth for free. The sand is sugar white and very soft, the water is crystal clear and very blue. There are plenty of beach chairs and free beach towels from the resort. Yes there were a few topless women on the beach. And they didn't think anything of it. There was no complete nudity, just topless women. If this offends you for some odd reason, either get over it or don't go to the beach. The beach market area can be as fun as you make it. No price is final. Have some fun and barter with these shopowners. If you don't want bothered as you're walking, just put up your hand and they will leave you alone. They will be pushy as much as you permit them to. If you seem like the type they can pester until you give in, they will. If you let them know that you're not interested, they will pretty much leave you alone. Again, if you don't want to deal with this, then don't go there. But if you're good at bartering, you can get some unbelievable bargains. We did.As far as excursions, we did the Outback Safari which was the best day we had. You really get to see how Dominicans live and work. It was a blast. We also did the catamaran to the private island for a day. That was also very nice and you see some of the most beautiful beaches. Stay away from Manati Park. This place has several violations for mistreating animals. The dolphins are kept in a small tank 24/7 and they are very overcrowded. Please boycott this park. If they go out of business, these sea creatures will be turned loose in the ocean where they belong.We paid $600 pp for 8 days 7 nights. It was a last minute deal. If you want save a bundle, book it within 2 weeks of leaving. In my opinion, we got way more than we expected.  
<Date>Oct 5, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved it We just back from this resort and it was great. The weather was beautiful-sunny, hot and in the high 80's close to 90. The food is excellent but then again I am not a picky eater at all. We never went hungry. The beach and pools are beatiful. There is a huge language barrier since most of the employees speak Spanish. I was happy to get someone who spoke English. Bring dollar bills since it's easier to work with but I am sure they will change your money. I preferred not to have any pesos since I didn't want to get stuck with them. Bargain and haggle with the guys at the beach shops since they will work with you. They do pressure you a bit but I told them that I didn't want any pressure. We dealt with one guy that we bought T-shirts from and he was excellent. I told him that I would come back after looking around which I did. I understand they are making a living but sometimes they are too much. If you have a price in mind, try and work with them. Stand your ground and don't give in. They most likely will come around. I was able to get a carton of Marlboro Lights for $12 (US). My fiance and I enjoy the beachy atmosphere so we laid low. We went on a paddleboat but it was too windy so we got stuck. I jumped in and freed the rope and we returned the boat. I wish the workers n the beach would have told us before we rented the boat but we can only live and learn. I suggest you bring extra toilet paper since the resort has some that feels like paper towels. Bring your own tissues and wash cloths since they don't provide any. I took the advice of some of the other reviewers and brought the maid a little plastic bag full of crayons, pencils, pads, soaps and hair clips. I left it for her the day before we left. It's a third world country so they are very appreciative of little gifts. If you want to make their day, I would recommend doing it. I bought some items at the $1 store and packed up in a little case. I didn't want anything in return but just to help out since they work very, very hard down there.One pool was being renovated and the workers were there for 12 hours during the day and night. We actually felt bad for them but they were doing a great job with the renovations.We took a picture with a little money from a photographer on the beach and the it came out good so we bought it for $6 which was reasonable I thought.We had an amazing relaxing 4 days/3 nights so I have no major complaints. We made the most out of it and did the best we could.We took a shuttle to the Barcelo Casino which isn't too big but they have slots and tables and it's nice and cold in there. We only spent $20 so no major loss there. We took a taxi back since the shuttle leaves and picks up every 3 hours. The last shuttle leaves at 10 pm and picks up at 1 am. We didn't want to stay that long so we took a $5 taxi and tipped him $2. He spoke no English but we did make it back to the resort. The Villas Resort has a mixture of Americans and Europeans. Some tourists were rude but that can happen anywhere at any time.I do recommend this resort but if you can learn some Spanish beforehand you are better off. I wish I knew more than a few obvious words.I do believe that the male workers were more friendly than the female workers but that was my own opinion and observation.They do need to have more nightlife and nightly shows. They have one at 10 pm and the disco opens from 11:30-3 am. We were in a room on the beach so we heard the music. It was great when the air conditioning kicked in so it drowned out the music. It's a nice, beachy, friendly atmosphere. The check in was a nightmare but we believe since it's a holiday weekend that the staff was overwhelmed and not enough rooms were available. Check out was a breeze though.For the price we paid $530 pp for 4 days/3 nights all inclusive was well worth it. It was a fun, relaxing time and much deserved rest. Just some sun, fun, beach and pool. That's all we needed and all we wanted.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved Bavaro Villas I have to say the poor reviews out there about this place are wrong!I have been to this resort 3 times now and I love it, it is priced fabulously! The rooms are average but really you're not there to sit in your room are you? You are right on the Bavaro beach which is to die for! Crystal clear water, you can snorkel right off your own beach, my husband and I bring our own from home, so you don't have to wait for equipment!The food is great, but I guess some are pickier than others, I have been to other resorts along the beach and yes there are 5 stars out there that you are paying allot more money for but really I don't see a huge difference some but not worth double the price!There is a market right on the beach and I have seen reviews of too expensive for souveniers! Are you nuts! You need to barter with them first, and I have always walked away with beautiful gifts to bring home to everyone I know they are such good deals. You do need to watch out and not buy cigars on the beach and the local travel agents at the resorts will warn you to, they are not the good ones, we found the best on a tour of a cigar factory, not a museum but the actual factory for amazing prices you can't get anywhere! ($50us)It is a poor country and we always tipped our maids in money or what we did was take things from home like, crayons for the kids, small lotions and things that are like luxury to them but everyday to us, let me tell you your service will skyrocket from this!We are returning for a 4th time this coming winter and can't wait, the entertainment team even know us now when we return...do we get that here???It's truly worht the great deals don't be afraid!

<Author>lonaldluck
<Content>Great Time, isolated in complex We stayed the week of July 23 thru July 30 2004. We has a great time, for the price you could not beat it. The food was not great but we expected the worse and we were surprised it was not too bad. We did not have any trouble getting drinks even four at a time. Some of the staff were grumpy but most were pleasant. We found very few americans but alot of europeans. Just a few tips, bring a beach umbrella(you'll be glad) none for rent. There are no close ATM machines and if you do find them they will give Dominican dollars. There are safes in the room but you need to pay $9.00 per week for the key and lock. If you go looking for deals on cigars forget it. Any cigar I found in the Domincan Republic can be bought for half the price in the USA. They do have beach towels and beach chairs. The beach was beautiful, very little shade. A trolley runs back and forth from the beach since it is quite a hike. Prices for souvenirs are very high. Have fun!

<Author>dyncor
<Content>Villas, Not Very Good:( My husband and I went to the Barcelo Villas for 7 nights from May 21st-28th with our two daughters (4 and 1) and my sister and her friend (both 19). I have been telling everyone the same thing its the most beautiful place I have visited, but probably my worse vacation. I have a long story, but I will try to make it short. Originally, I booked this trip back in Feb 2004 off an early bird special for $679 pp (not including taxes) so I thought it was great for 7 nights, but come May when my sister booked it the price dropped to $379 pp. I felt so ripped off I contacted the travel agency (Apple Vacations) but no refund offered due to not having bought travel insurance (don't know what that has to do with higher price?). Anyway, that was a sign of the bad trip ahead. At the airport (BWI) we had a seven-hour delay on USA 3000. I am surprised to not have seen any reviews from some of the passengers but we are still trying to recuperate from the trip. Reason for the delay, no plane. It was a wasted day with no explanation from Apple Vacations and a lot of frustration from the passengers, at least we gotbreakfast vouchers. Instead of arriving at breakfast we got to Punta Cana at dinner. We also had a four-hour delay on our return trip (talk about throwing salt to injury), again no plane. They gave our plane away and hoped we would get another. It was so hard at the airport with two small children. I wrote a letter to Apple Vacations consumer affairs and just got back $100 Apple Vacation gift certificates each to use on our next trip. Punta Cana is a beautiful place. It is a very poor country, but the beach is absolutely breath-taking with 40 foot palm trees all the way down to the water. The first two days we were there the beach was extremely windy (sand going in our eyes) and the water was too cold. I thought this sucks, I came all the way here and I can't swim. Turns out the worse devastation to strike DR occurred on Monday when flooding killed thousands of people along a river bordering DR and Haiti. It was all over the news and flags flew at half-staff. After that the beach was no longer windy and the water became warm. The only thing I didn't like about Punta Cana, is that you can't leave the resort. It鈥檚 not safe. You are basically trapped if you do not do excursions. We went to Manati Park (fun shows and great animals) highly recommended. PC, is not likeCancun where you can walk around town or take a bus and go out on your own. There is no city to visit unless you want to go to Romana or Santa Domingo (too far). You are stuck in the resort. Now, if the resort was great that would not be a problem, but this was in the states what you would call a 2 star at best. Let me start with the rooms. As you have read on previous reviews the hotel layout is narrow going away from the ocean. The Ocean Village is the closest to the ocean, than the Village and than all the way in the back (I mean all the way) is the Villas. The ones all the way in the back are 30 minutes to the beach (I timed it) but they are for the staff and not for guests. The staff works 11 days straight and goes home for 3 days. So, its about 15-20 minutes at the beginning of the Villas. If you don't mind Geckos and a long walk stay at the Villas, but we had small children so the Village worked well. We were ready with our tip to get a better room at the Villas and to my surprise we got a room in the Village. The front desk would not accept a tip. I gave him American candy, he seemed surprised. The room seemed great, it was right in front of the Village pool (very shallow and great for small children) and directly in front of the snack bar. We always got pizza first. Our room turned out to be infested with everything possible. We started with mosquitoes, moths, biting ants and than cockroaches ranging from babies to extremely large. I threw away my husbands flip-flops b/c he killed so many and now he is mad at me b/c he liked them so much. It was really bad guys. I walked around with shoes all the time. I left our area to get away from the cicadas (17-yearlocust hitting Mid-Atlantic States) and came back not afraid. I literally killed 20 bugs a day and my husband, God knows how many. The worse was when the ants crawled up to our beds (we moved the beds away from the wall) or when the extremely large cockroaches got away and we could not catch them. I had nightmares that they would crawl up on me. I told my husband about some of the reviewers stating they had bugs but, I didn't think it would be a problem and he was mad that we stayed there. My sister and her friend on the other hand did not have any bugs in there room, but a monkey outside their balcony that wokethem up at 8am every morning. The big problem was that we could not be out all day in the sun with small children and we could not stay in theroom b/c of all the bugs. By the time we finished killing everything, the next day the maid would leave the doors open while cleaning and more would get in. Believe me we never opened the balcony door and or let things in, but there were definitely some holes around the room that were letting them in. One lady told us she had a spider living in her mattress that bit her so bad she had to go to the doctor on site for injections for her swelling. They charged her $100 for each visit. Hope you get a room with no bugs. At least this experience has made me tough.I was looking forward to the eating out everyday b/c I was tired of cooking at home and needed a break. I would have been happy with anything, but I actually was happy to be home again. I can't believe I said that, but the food was pretty bad. I never went hungry but I didn't like the selections. I ate mostly bread (tons of it on the buffet) and fruits. Please take Imodium with you; all of us (except the kids-thank goodness) got traveler's sickness. If it weren鈥檛 for Imodium we would be stuck in our room the whole time. My husband didn't say much about the food; he just didn't eat too much. The teenagers hated it and my small children ate it but pushed most things aside. My husband is from South American and I from the Middle East so we are familiar with non-American food. We love food from all over the world; it was not that, it just wasn't good. Also, the one restaurant was closed down the week wewere there for renovations so we only had three to pick from. The restaurants do not have doors and windows so the bugs get in, especially the one near the Villas. The food is directly in front ofthe open space. I got to a point where I pushed the bug (still alive) off my plate and continued eating. The drinks are pretty watered down so be prepared (coke taste like coke+water and pina colada tastes as bad as the ones I make at home). I still drank them. The entertainment was great, really funny contests, but some nights it was the same and we left early. We went to the disco a couple of nights and it was okay. The staff is friendly, some too flirtatious with my sister and her friend. Theygot annoying after a while. Beware of the markets on the beach, you do not get much of a bargain, just hassle. I went once and never returned, I don't like pushy people and shopped at the gift stores. My sister and her friend got a lot of stuff and some stuff for the same price I did. They give you tons of free necklaces though. Be careful buying cigars too, we got stopped at BWI. We bought DR cigars but the one cop said they were grown from the cochiba seed which is from Cuba so we have to throw them away. Than the head cop said it was okay b/c it was made in the DR. They made some lady throw away $600 of cochiba cigars. Tips: If you can, don't bring babies or children under 2 years old, hahaha...Ours ate sand all day, didn't like eating at restaurants and didn't let us have a good time. The hotel is old and if it wasn't for the great landscaping it would not be very nice. I noticed it was the least expense hotel in the Punta Cana, so don't be surprised. Upgrade to a better hotel if you can, seriously. I agreed with most of the advice on the other reviews except tip with money not gifts. I left a different gift everyday for our maids and to other workers and they all looked at me funny. The gifts were worth more than a few dollars, but money works best for them. I would go to Punta Cana again but never, neverstay at this hotel again. On the way home, all the other passengers raved about their hotels and all of us at the Barcelo stayed quiet. I don't believe you get what you paid for b/c I paid double what other people did for the same hotel, but read reviews and check the internet before making a reservation here. We were ready to go home by the second day, but we stuck it out and we definitely had good times as well as bad times. Make the best of your trip and have fun as we tried to do!!!:)

<Author>oliver2616
<Content>Beautiful My husband and I just returned from 7 nights at the Barcelo Villas Bavaro, Dominican Republic. I would not use Charm City Travel again. We flew into La Romana airport which is an hour and a half ride from the resort. This was nice because you got to see a few towns and some of the country. We flew on USA 3000 airlines. Great airline. Nice planes and we got food.  The resort is beautiful with flowers and Palm Trees everywhere. It is also very large. The rooms were plain but clean. The air conditioning worked very well and there was plenty of very hot water. The pool by the Villas is the largest and prettiest. There is a stage near the pool where there is nightly entertainment. Around 7:30 or 8:00 pm there are clowns to entertain the children and the adult show starts around 10:00 pm. The Villas are about a 10 to 15 minute walk to the beach which was great, giving us a chance to walk off all the food we ate. You walk past three pools and bars on the way. The food was better than I expected. A large variety at every meal and Pizza and hot dogs at the pool by the lobby at 3:30. There was ice cream and many desserts. The people were very friendly although they didn't speak very much English, but we managed to communicate with some Spanish words I had printed from the internet. The tour guides at the hotel and on excursions spoke English very well.We took the Jungle Safari tour which was about $70.00 a person. We visited a Dominican mid-income home, a cattle ranch where we had lunch, a place where they grow coffee and cocoa beans, a school and a public beach where we went boogie boarding. Our guide, Alex, made Cuba Libras (rum and coke) and Champagna (sprite and rum) on the whole trip. There was also Cervaza (beer) and soda and water. All included in the price as was lunch. It was a lot fun and interesting to see the countryside and get a feel for the country. We also took a speedboat snorkeling tour, $50.00. This was a lot of fun.Unless you like to be on the beach or at the pool, or play volleyball there isn't much to do at the resort. There are a lot of other things to do (tours) but they will cost extra. There is also a Casino which we didn't get to go to. Of course you can always sit by the bars.Bring a lot of $1.00 bills. You will need these for tipping. These people are very poor and the tips really help them We didn't change our money into pesos and had no trouble. Most places gave us US dollars in change. At the time we were there (June 5th - 12th) it was 48 pesos to the US dollar but it changes daily.It was hot but there was usually a breeze. The beach is gorgeous. There is not much shade on the beach and no umbrellas. The Palm trees are very tall and provide enough shade for two lounge chairs, which you have to keep moving with the sun. You need Sun Screen 40 or 50. We had to buy it there and it is very expensive. One of the stores wanted $26.00 for it. Bring it along. There is a small store near the pool closest to the beach where they will bargain so I got a small bottle of sunscreen for $15.00. Also bring washcloths. There aren't any.There was a little rain, but not much. It rained mostly at night. Really no problem with bugs; a few ants on the porch.We met a lot of nice people. There are people from many countries; England, Russia, Germany, France, Spanish speaking countries and the US. It was well worth the money.

<Content>Vacation from hell... My girlfriend and I traveled to This resort on May 10-17 2004, boy we thought we got a really good deal off the internet. --- We were mistaken! When we arrived our room was not ready when they initially told us it would be, not really a big problem, but it gets worse. After we got settled in we inspected the room to find rust in the shower, dirt on the floor, and a maid that could not understand a word of english. We decided to go for a few drinks at the pool bar--JOKE, they ignored you as if, they didn't see us, I had to get out of the pool to wait another 10 minutes to get a drink. Everytime I was waited on, they paused for a minute expecting a tip. I'm not cheep and this is All-Inclusive, but fair is fair and I tiped thinking it would increase there attention in my direction, and the drinks would be much easier to get,NOPE. They just took the tip and went about their business taking their good old time with other requests. I spoke to one of the travel agents down there and he said that they work 11 staight days with 11 hour shifts, then they get off for three days, soo that's why they are soo grumpy. I realized by the end of the trip that this is not a vacation for Americans, they tend to favor, Germans, French, Dustchland and pretty much any other European Native. On top[ of that if you are an average American who does not speak any spanish, this resort is not for you. On the beach, they never had any snorkel equiptment. They response would be  5 minitos, an hour later they are still saying 5 minitos! In conclusion; The Island is beautiful, the people suck, and the food sucks!!! My advice would be to bring alot of snacks, don't go to this resort, pay a few more hundred dollars and brush up on you Spanish! Good luck and I hope this helped you in your decision.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Take your own food!!! Just got back last night from Barcelo Villas after a 3 night mini-trip. All I can say is this place was a major disappointment. I knew going into it that it would not be THE RITZ, but I never expected what I found. The grounds and rooms were adequate, but we were in the #1200 villas which are as far as you can be from the beach (3/4 mile), pools, etc. They have guards with long sticks and guns draped over their chests who lurk around at night and make obscene gestures at you (there were 4 females on our trip) while standing 4 feet from your patio. I called the front desk to ask them to remove this guard from standing there because we were frightened and I was told they are there to provide a service. What a bonus for us! One of my friends twisted her ankle and we called the desk about 10 times in 2 hours to get her some ice. It seemed that there are only few people who can speak English at this resort and no ice ever arrived. I had to walk all the way to the reception, speak in my poor Spanish, just to procure ice after finally asking for the manager.As for the food, we were all repulsed -- choices were goat stew, lamb ragout, rabbit. After seeing those items, I was not going to trust something marked beef on the buffet. I lived on pizza at 3:30 everyday which was served at the main pool as my one and only food for 4 days!!! All of the alcohol was Normandy brand and the top shelf drinks were more than you would pay for them in NYC. The Presidente beer that was served on tapwas not all that bad, but it wasn't all that good either. They actually sold it in the stores on the hotel premises for 50 pesos a 6 pack. Funny, but 44 pesos is equivalent to $1US, so that pretty much explains the beer. I haven't drank such cheap beer since my college days!My two biggest grips are the hospitality you do NOT receive and the lack of bottled water. We did get a hint from another guest that a bartender guy named Sandy at the Margarita Bar was excellent and attentive once you tipped him. I gave him $10 one night and my friend gave him $5 the next so he was one of the few people who was actually attentive to us, most usually ignored us. As for water it is hit or miss, somethimes the bars have bottled water and sometimes not. Plus in the resturants you are always served tap water. Needless to say, 2 of us on the trip both had to visit our doctors today for a mega dose of z-pak to get rid of the bacteria that found its way into our bodies if you get my point.I have traveled extensively in the Carribean, Meditterean and Mexico and would not return to this resort if they paid me to visit it! We did manage to create our own fun and met some great people to hang out with and go to the disco later at night which is really fun, but hot since it is outside. At the disco they also never had bottled water.A word of caution for American families considering going here -- do keep in mind that most of the clientele is European so there will be a majority of the women on the beach going topless while wearing thongs. I am used to this and realize it is their culture, but I did speak to some people who were appalled with it.Take the snorkeling trip from the beach for $13 though. The fish on the reef are plentiful, but there are not as many different types as you would see in the Caymans or Mexico, but make sure they take you out to the caged sharks. That was cool swimming with them, and the variety of fish there is much greater.Next time I can book a trip so cheaply, I will pass and pay more for a higher rated hotel as people on our plane were raving about their 5 and 6 star hotels!!!!
